Turkey Requests Revision of the Treaty of Lausanne to Abolish the Demilitarization Clauses of the Straits 47

(London) The Treaty of Lausanne, signed by the major powers and Turkey in 1923, stipulates that the shores of the Bosporus and Dardanelles straits are demilitarized zones. According to the Daily Telegraph, the Turkish government has recently made representations to the governments of European countries on this matter, requesting that the clauses on the demilitarization of the Treaty of Lausanne be abolished, so that the Turkish government can maintain its neutrality in the event of war in the future. According to the newspaper, most governments, except for the signatories of the Balkan Pact and Soviet Russia, have expressed opposition to Turkey's request. (Havas Telegram, 23rd)

Natural and Man-Made Disasters in Europe: Spain Again Has Riots and Bloodshed, France Reduces Government Spending and Leftists Demonstrate, Yugoslavia Mine Explosion 48

Madrid: The streets of Madrid are very chaotic today. Police and extremists clashed in various places, with gunfire flying. As a result, one person was killed and many were injured. Strikers, revolutionaries, and communists threw many bombs, creating a terrible Sunday. Many churches, monasteries and public buildings were destroyed by fire. The police repeatedly drove away the rebels, but Madrid has been severely disturbed. All factories have stopped work. The political circles are now very worried, because if there is another day of strike, the whole city will feel the lack of bread. At the same time, there have been many riots in various cities in Spain. Spanish Prime Minister Lerroux insisted on the policy of suppressing the chaos. According to the report at 6:00 PM today, the police occupied the roofs and fought against the rebels, firing 200 shots. Two churches were burned, and the fire illuminated the sky. In the city of Aencola, 40,000 people rioted and fired many shots, but no deaths or injuries have been reported. (National Telegram, 22nd)

Madrid: Yesterday's riots due to the strike killed one person and injured five people, including a young man from London named Taylor, who was shot in the head and chest. He came here to study Spanish for only two weeks after winning a travel award. Great losses were caused to property in the city. A nunnery was set on fire by violent acts and destroyed. A large hotel was set on fire by a bomb and burned to the ground. A total of 120 people were arrested in the riot. Although the Minister of Interior issued a public notice last night, the situation is still very serious. The police are very vigilant, because they are often subjected to various snipers on the road, and some people shoot remotely from the roof. It is now feared that as a result of the riots, the president may refuse to sign the amnesty for political prisoners passed by Congress on Friday. If so, it will inevitably cause a cabinet crisis. (Reuters Telegram, 23rd)

(Paris) The National Communist Party and the Socialist Party are staging demonstrations against the government's pay cuts. Today, Finance Minister Mandante issued a statement stating the reasons for the government's austerity policy, saying that the government, in the face of financial difficulties, wants to avoid defaulting on its debts, and there are only three possible coping methods: (1) borrowing money, (2) lowering the value of the currency, and (3) saving money to balance revenue and expenditure. Lowering the value of the currency is not feasible, and borrowing money cannot be done, because France needs to borrow at a 6% interest rate, while Britain only needs 2.5%. The current high cost of living must be fundamentally eliminated and adjusted by prudent and gradual methods. The root causes are (1) interest rates are too high, (2) taxes are too heavy, and (3) railway fares are extremely high. The Finance Minister also said that the government's policy will now allow the large sums of money engaged in hoarding due to the instability of the situation to circulate in the market, thereby increasing purchasing power. Before the Finance Minister issued this article, French Prime Minister Doumergue gave a sincere radio address, asking the people of the country to unite and stop the disputes. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

Belgrade: A gas explosion in the Kakangi coal mine in Yugoslavia killed 200 people. 162 people have been found, but only 15 people working at the entrance of the mine were rescued alive, and the rest died. There are still 38 people buried deep in the mine, and there is no hope of survival. (Reuters Telegram, 22nd)

The Volume of International Arms Trading is Very Large: Total Value of US$5.5 Billion in Ten Years, with the Largest Amount of Shipments in the Year Before Last 49

(New York) According to statistics on the world's exports of arms and military supplies in the past ten years, the total value is US$5 billion, with the largest amount of arms shipments in 1932. In addition to finished military supplies, there are also many raw materials, such as nitrates, which have equal value in peacetime and wartime. In recent months, Chile's nitrate exports have soared, mostly transported through the Panama Canal to the East. From January to November 1922, aircraft exports from the United States were 67% higher than the total amount in the previous year. The Curtis-Wright factory shipped aircraft to Soviet Russia, Japan, China, Germany, Spain, the Netherlands, France, Italy, Switzerland, Czechoslovakia, Bulgaria, and South American countries last year. The US Navy purchased 1,100 aircraft, and the Army Department ordered more than 1,800 aircraft. The explosives sold by DuPont Company in 1933 increased by 24% compared to 1932. The revenue in 1932 was US$23,363,000, and it increased to US$37,262,000 last year. According to DuPont Company, it supplied 80% of the arms to the Allied powers during the Great War. The United Kingdom and the United States have now decided to build warships in accordance with the limits of the naval treaty. A member of the Japanese parliament requested two months ago to levy a special tax on military factories, which is said to be "the most prosperous industry in today's Japanese industry." According to the Chronicle of Japan on January 6, the military supplies imported in 1931 amounted to 778,867 Japanese yen, and increased to 6,452,077 yen in 1933. The import volume of special steel was 884,981 yen in 1931, and it jumped to 4,465,018 yen in 1933. According to the report of the International Nickel Company of Canada, the profit in 1933 was 9,662,583 yuan, which is incomparable to the loss of 135,344 yuan in 1932. Nickel is the main raw material of arms. The Cinatre-Krisso Company of France manages 412 arms manufacturing plants in France, the Little Entente, and the Balkans. Compared with the Wickham-Armstrong Company of the United Kingdom, the arsenals in the United States are still small. (National Telegram, 22nd)

This invention of Soviet scientists has aroused the warm interest of microbiologists around the world. Several well-known foreign societies (such as the Lister Institute in the United Kingdom, etc.) have applied to the Experimental Medical Research Institute for explanations of this method in order to prepare for the production of serum in accordance with the law.

Hayashi Senjūrō's Resignation is Closely Related to Hirota's Statement (Japanese Dispatch) 85

Military Policy Achieves Another Victory

China Policy to Become More Aggressive

The resignation of Army Minister Hayashi Senjūrō is ostensibly due to his younger brother, Shirokami Yūkichi, being convicted of bribery, for which he feels deeply responsible. However, the reality is not so simple. Of course, Hayashi Senjūrō, to maintain his image as a military statesman, could not but express his resignation. However, there is an unprecedented miracle regarding the Cabinet of Japan this time: when he tendered his resignation, he did not recommend a successor as Army Minister.

According to the long-standing customs of the Japanese Cabinet organization, the Army Minister has special powers. He is considered a member of the political party cabinet, but does not advance or retreat with the political party cabinet. His source is not a recommendation from the political party when forming the cabinet, but rather a result of consultations among the three leaders of the army (i.e., Chief of Staff, Inspector General of Military Education, and Minister of the Army), who then recommend him to the cabinet head. The Prime Minister has absolutely no power to refuse or negotiate a replacement. The Saitō Makoto Cabinet was a mixed-party cabinet, and Saitō himself was a senior figure in the navy, so problems in the navy seemed unlikely. However, the army caused him headaches. The reason for the Army Minister's resignation this time is very legitimate, and his attitude is very firm. If he were to truly resign, the cabinet would be in an extremely difficult position, because the successor Army Minister should be nominated when the current Army Minister resigns, but this has not been done. Leaving it like this would make the current cabinet very embarrassed.

There are various complex relationships behind the scenes of this Army Minister's resignation. First, since the beginning of this year, the struggle between the militarists and the capitalists has been extremely fierce, extending from the South Manchurian Railway reorganization issue to domestic and foreign affairs, especially diplomatic relations with the United States, Britain, and China, and also with the Soviet Union. However, Japan's preparations for war with the Soviet Union have long been commonly acknowledged by the capitalists. It is only the other diplomatic relations, especially with China, that are at issue. The capitalists advocate a moderate diplomacy, advocating economic goodwill. The militarists believe that military needs should be the basis, and diplomacy should follow military shifts, even with Britain and the United States. Second, the middle-ranking officers in the military strongly advocate the continued implementation of a tough policy, and absolutely cannot allow other countries to interfere in China, nor can they allow China to lean towards pro-British and pro-American stances. Third, they see that China is consistently approaching the League of Nations, such as technical cooperation, as well as silver companies, and the development of aviation, all of which have international entanglements. Aviation in particular is a step that Japan fears, so the military demands that the government have a concrete and definitive expression, an expression of a tough policy. Otherwise, the military will take actions uncooperative with the cabinet. Not recommending a successor Army Minister is one aspect of this. Therefore, since Army Minister Hayashi's resignation on the 11th of this month, the cabinet has been very panicked, the financial capitalists have been very uneasy, and the various political parties feel that a great disaster is looming. If there is no way to mediate, whether Araki Sadao is reappointed as Army Minister, or even a military cabinet is realized, then the so-called constitutional politics will come to an end from now on, and the capitalists will have to go to the military to make a living. Fortunately, the Saitō Cabinet painstakingly mended the situation. After being comforted by the Chief of Staff, Hayashi Senjūrō decided to revoke his resignation and resume his post. On the 18th of this month, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an unofficial statement, expressing his intention to monopolize the Chinese market and the meaning of the East Asian Monroe Doctrine. The main reason why the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued this statement was to quell internal discontent, and at the same time to take the opportunity to probe the attitudes of the United States and Britain. The military's opinion still supports its traditional thinking, believing that the United States is struggling in an economic panic, Britain is just beginning to recover, and has no spare capacity, the Soviet Union will definitely not help China, and Europe itself is in a time of multiple events, and has no time to look east. Taking this opportunity to put pressure on China, seize the entire market, or at least control North China, is a very advantageous approach. However, the government has two preparations: one is to comply with the military's demands, while at the same time strengthening the capitalists' front, and the other is to examine the international atmosphere, and continue to strive for the US-Japan alliance movement, to make the United States understand Japan's position, and prepare for the demand for naval equality, as a step for future exchange. After all, this statement is just a prelude, and the real drama is yet to come. (April 19th, Tokyo)

Gold and Silver: London Gold Price Today (April 23)

The London gold price is 135 shillings and 7.5 pence, down half a penny.

London Bullion Today (April 23): The London silver market opened steadily. Spot is 19 pence 875, futures are 19 pence 9375, both up one eighth of a penny. Indian buying in the morning, some selling, but demand from buyers is high, and the close is sluggish.

New York Bullion Today (April 23): The silver market opened mixed. Hopes for the White Silver Act are fading, and silver prices are trending downward. Sales are still not high at this time. Although the market situation was calmer in the morning, because there is no certainty about the future, the recent outlook is very bleak. Operators are now closely watching developments in Washington. At the opening of the futures market, prices fell by 0 to 5 points compared to the closing price on Saturday and Sunday, but January was long by 5 points.

However, when prices fell, retail investors, peers, Liverpool, and Europe bought in. Later, due to unfavorable news from Liverpool, higher dollar prices, favorable weather reports, and uncertain silver developments, cotton prices fell again.

Indian Cotton: The Bombay cotton market fell initially today (April 23) due to speculation by speculators, followed by a slight recovery due to purchases by some exporters. The July-August price of white Roch cotton was 196 rupees 75, down half a rupee.

English Cotton: The Liverpool cotton market was looser today (April 23). At 1:00 PM, the price for July was 5.83, down 4 points. English Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market was at 1:00 PM today (April 23). The price for July was 4 shillings 3 pence 75, which was lower than the closing price on Saturday and Sunday by .625.

New York Today (April 23): The rubber market situation is active, because London is firm and there are rumors that restrictive measures are expected to be implemented soon. However, profit-taking has blocked the upward trend.

Northern Fujian War Concentrates in Jiangle and Yong'an - Wei Lihuang Has Returned to Fujian - 91

Fuzhou Dispatch: After the Red bandits from eastern Jiangxi infiltrated northern Fujian, they captured Jiangle from Jianning, advanced towards Yong'an from Qingliu, and used small detachments to harass Shaxian's Xiamao and Nanping's Wangtai. The 10th Column Commander of the Eastern Route Army, Tang Enbo, stationed troops from [illegible] and other divisions in Tai Ning, Mingxi, Shaxian, Yong'an, and Shunchang counties. Fierce battles have been taking place with the bandits in recent days. It is learned that the bandits in the Jiangle and Wangtai areas belong to Peng Dehuai's forces, and the bandits in the Yong'an and Xiamao areas belong to Luo Binghui's forces. The Eastern Route Army is using [illegible] two divisions to attack Jiangle from Tai Ning and Shunchang. The offensive began on the 11th, advancing from the border of Tai Ning's Shuinan and the border of Shunchang's Wan'an to Xikou and Liangfang across the stream from the county seat. The bandits have set up defensive works in the suburbs to resist. [illegible] two divisions have surrounded them. In Yong'an, [illegible] two divisions have also surrounded them. Yong'an ordered the [illegible] division to firmly defend the city and wait for reinforcements. According to a telegram from [illegible] Division Commander yesterday, the bandit forces in the Hufang and Xinkou areas have been defeated. [illegible] division also sent troops to attack from both sides. The bandit forces were unable to resist and showed signs of fleeing towards Ningyang and Liancheng in western Fujian. The Fuzhou Headquarters immediately telegraphed Eastern Route Army Commander-in-Chief Jiang Dingwen, ordering 4th Column Commander Li Yannian to quickly advance towards Ningyang and Liancheng to intercept. As for the scattered bandits harassing Wangtai and Xiamao, 9th Column Commander Liu Heding has dispatched troops from Nanping and Shaxian to suppress them, and they should be cleared within days. Furthermore, Eastern Route Frontline Commander-in-Chief Wei Lihuang returned to Fujian on the Jiesheng steamship from Shanghai on the 19th. He will lead the Frontline Headquarters personnel to Yanping within days to preside over military affairs in northern Fujian. (April 20th)

Chao-Shan's Newlywed Tax, Peanut Tax of Two Yuan per Month, Also Actually Solicited for Merchant Contracts 93

Shantou Dispatch: In addition to the provincial national tax, the Chao-Mei counties also have local taxes levied by police districts or security groups, which are extremely harsh and detailed. For example, in Zhanglin Town, Chenghai County, the district office recently announced that the various donations from last year have expired, and specially solicited merchants on the 10th to openly bid for the continuation of business. The monthly amount of donations from each merchant is recorded below: Chicken, Goose, and Duck Donation: 27 yuan, 3 jiao, and 3 he, won by Gongsi; Newlywed Donation: 24 yuan and 8 jiao, won by Heyu Shun Company; Firewood Donation: 42 yuan, 7 jiao, and 5 fen, won by Yihe Company; Banquet Donation: 41 yuan, 7 jiao, and 2 fen, won by Pingan Branch; Peanut Donation: 2 yuan per month, won by Yushun Company; Stream Front Porter Donation: 7 yuan, 4 jiao, and 5 fen per month, won by Yuemei Company; Charcoal Donation: 11 yuan and 5 jiao per month, won by Yuemei Company; Pig Broker Commission Donation: 28 yuan, 1 jiao, and 1 fen, won by Yushun. (17th)

Northwest Inspection Record by Our Special Correspondent Geng Ya

New Suiyuan Automobile Route Scenery 94

In the newly developed transportation of Xinjiang and the inland regions, the New Suiyuan long-distance bus service, renowned for its remarkable achievements and high reputation, has its main station in Suiyuan. We visited Director Mou Pengling of the station, who warmly welcomed us and engaged in extensive discussions. Director Mou, originally involved in education in the Northeast, joined the company and traveled to Xinjiang, providing valuable insights into the conditions along the route. He mentioned that Xinjiang's land is vast and the situation precarious, making it difficult to gain a deep understanding without personally visiting. While the New Suiyuan automobile route holds significant commercial and economic value, its strategic importance for national defense is far less than the Gansu-Xinjiang line. This is because the New Suiyuan line is close to Outer Mongolia and easily susceptible to external threats, whereas the Gansu-Xinjiang line is like a vital artery that urgently needs to be cleared. The New Suiyuan line spans 5,980 Chinese miles from Suiyuan to Dihua. The terrain along the route is mostly flat and passable, except for Wugongba, which has a steep gradient. In areas like Bailing Temple, Haiya Amatu, Saihutun, and Heishatu, there are many soft sandy rivers. In Mailinggen and other places, there are numerous Cogon grass mounds. In places like Chahandian ceremony and Keketaolaigai, there are many mountain valleys and gullies. West of Keketaolaigai, water is scarce and tastes bitter, making travel difficult, but these obstacles can be overcome with manpower. Westward from Suiyuan, the residents of Wuchuan are engaged in both agriculture and animal husbandry, with the Han people primarily engaged in agriculture and the Mongolian people primarily engaged in animal husbandry. Further northwest to Bailing Temple, there are over ten Mongolian and Han shops, serving as the gateway for entering and exiting Inner Mongolia from the Northwest. Beyond this point, villages become scarce, and human habitation is rare. One might encounter nomadic Mongolians with only two or three families every seven or eight hundred miles. The journey is characterized by desolate wilderness, continuous mountains, and vast ravines, with winding and rugged sandy terrain. One can imagine the difficulties in driving and equipment. Upon reaching Hami, villages and towns become commonplace. Places such as Gu Chengzi and Dihua are bustling commercial hubs with larger populations compared to other areas. The rugged mountain paths and the impassable stretches of sand dunes and quicksand rivers along the route should be prioritized for repair and construction, followed by other sections, to ensure the completion of a solid highway. Mr. Bai Xuchu, a director of the company from Xinjiang, was also present. He said that the Northwest provinces are arid and receive little rainfall, but the snow on the Tianshan Mountains in Xinjiang melts and irrigates the fields like gushing springs, resulting in lush water and grass, suitable for both farming and grazing. The main mineral resources, particularly in northern Xinjiang, are abundant with gold, silver, iron, tungsten, coal, oil, crystal, salt, and other materials. Furthermore, the jade of Hetian in southern Xinjiang is renowned both domestically and internationally. If the Chinese people do not unite to develop this great land and its limitless resources, it is highly likely that we will repeat the mistakes made in the Northeast. Later, the company insisted on hosting a banquet and invited over ten members of the press, including Lin Chaoran, Yang Lingde, and Wang Xizhou, to accompany them. During the banquet, they expressed their sincerity and welcomed guidance.

The newspaper industry in Suiyuan is quite developed, with two major newspapers, the Suiyuan Daily (government-run) and the Suiyuan Republic Daily (party-run). There are also smaller newspapers like the Social Daily (Department of Education), the Morning Post (related to the Party Headquarters), and the recently published Industrial Daily. News agencies include the Suiyuan News Agency, the Suiyuan News Service, the Saibei News Agency, the Northwest News Agency, and the Guihua News Agency. All of these are located in the provincial capital. In other counties, only Baotou has the Baotou Daily and the Bianwen News Agency. Some individuals are eager to establish another newspaper that truly represents the people's voice, but due to financial difficulties, they are unable to realize it at this time.

Since Suiyuan was opened as a commercial port in the third year of the Republic and the entire PingSui Railway was opened to traffic, commercial prosperity has increased day by day, needless to say. However, since the Outer Mongolian incident, traffic has been cut off, tea and cloth cannot be sold, and fur and hides are blocked from sources. The blow to commerce is almost the same as that of Zhangjiakou. Fortunately, prices are low and it is still easy for ordinary people to make a living. Mr. Yang Lingde (chief editor of the Suiyuan News Agency) served local flavor drinks one after another, which were rich and delicious, and the price was cheap and good, which is truly worthy. Moreover, there are no bad habits of using female receptionists like in Pingjin Zhangjiakou. I once took a rickshaw, the cushions and backrests were made of flannel, and the footrests were covered with plush carpets, which was more luxurious than private cars in Shanghai. The daily rental price is only two or three jiao, and the rickshaw driver earns two or three jiao a day, which is enough for a family of five. For example, students in Pingjin need six or seven yuan a month for food, but three yuan is enough here.

The tomb of Han Mingfei Zhao Jun is located twenty miles south of the city, on the bank of the Dahei River. The surrounding fields are fertile. Five or six miles out of the city, the road passes through sandy land, the car travels silently, the spokes rise and the sand spills out, like a mill spitting out powder. Looking ahead, the "Green Tomb" rises prominently in the distance, its color is verdant, but it is still more than ten miles away. The tomb is eight or nine zhang high and is circular facing south. There are six public stone tablets erected on the flat ground, all built since the end of the Qing Dynasty and the Republic of China. There is a winding path to the west that can be climbed. There is an earthen cave on it, with a bell and earthen figurines, called the Daxian Temple (ie Fox Immortal), which the village children worship. Broken tiles and bricks can be seen at the tomb site, and it is estimated that there must have been temples and words in previous generations. On the return trip, we visited the first spring on the Nine Borders (ancient Wuliang Temple) and several other Lama temples. The situation is similar to Huaping Yonghe Palace and Nanjing Confucius Temple. Lama temples are commonly called "Zhao". Shops are set up in the buildings, but business is not prosperous. There is also a Bing in front of "Dazhao," with eight mouths a day, called Yuquan Water (ie Kangxi's inscription "First Spring on the Nine Borders"), which residents take and draw from. The street east of the spring is called South Street, which is very lively. Yang Lingde took full responsibility as a guide, and his deep friendship and enthusiasm were touching.

The New Suiyuan Automobile Company is preparing for its third westward journey, but the date has not yet been determined. Therefore, the reporter will still follow the original plan and go to Ninggan first. Mr. Huipin heard about it and made a special trip to visit him. The most worrying thing is that bandits often appear along the way. If you encounter them, the best way to deal with it is to be alert. The first important thing is to make them not suspect that I am resisting, remember, remember. Secondly, the climate in the places you pass is cold and dry, and you must be prepared with clothing and medicines, etc. The borderland inspection passport issued internally has been transferred by Director Yan of the Department of Education, and should be stamped by the provincial government. I will go to Baotou tomorrow (17th).

Min River: Sailing Ships and Steamships Compete for Transportation 95

#### Steamship Association Petitions Party and Government Authorities

Fuzhou Correspondence: The Min River, the largest waterway in Fujian, originates from the Luxi and Guangze counties on the border of Fujian and Jiangxi. It flows through Shaowu, Shunchang, and Nanping, dividing into three branches: east, north, and west. The north branch flows from Nanping through Jian'ou and Pucheng, entering Zhejiang Province. The west branch flows from Nanping to Shaxian. The east branch flows from Nanping through Gutian, Minqing, and Minhou, entering the sea. Before the opening of maritime trade, it was a vital route between Zhejiang and Jiangxi provinces. Previously, sailing ships navigated the river. It is estimated that there were no fewer than a thousand sailing ships of various sizes, supporting the livelihoods of tens of thousands of boatmen. In recent years, merchants and travelers, in order to develop transportation, have pooled funds to purchase steamships, which have become increasingly popular. Over a decade, the number of steamships has grown from a few to over a hundred. Passengers and cargo shippers have abandoned sailing ships in favor of steamships, severely impacting the livelihoods of boatmen. In the 16th year of the Republic of China, they organized the Civil Boatmen's Union, seeking to engage in a showdown with the steamships. The situation on the Min River was extremely dangerous. Steamships were at risk of being destroyed by the Civil Boatmen's Union. Steamship merchants also organized the Steamship Association, requesting military protection. This stalemate lasted for two years, resulting in significant losses for both sides and severely hindering commercial transportation. In the 18th year of the Republic of China, party and government authorities intervened as arbitrators, agreeing to revise the agreement. The three types of goods transported from the upper reaches of the Min River (i.e., northern Fujian) to the lower reaches (i.e., Fuzhou)—tea, paper, and bamboo shoots—and the three types of goods transported from the lower reaches of the Min River to the upper reaches—powdered salt, rice, and vermicelli—were all to be transported by sailing ships. The navigation routes of steamships were also restricted. The North Stream was only allowed to navigate to Jian'ou, the West Stream to Shaxian, and the Central Stream to Yangkou. Beyond these points, the river becomes shallow and rapid, making navigation impossible. This arrangement allowed for a period of relative peace. In the 21st year of the Republic of China, the arbitration period expired, and disputes arose again between the two sides. Party and government authorities extended the agreement for another two years. At the end of March this year, the agreement expired for the second time. Steamships, no longer restricted, began to transport all types of goods. On April 1st, the Civil Boatmen's Union gathered a large number of boatmen at the Hongshan Bridge on the Min River outside the West Gate of Fuzhou. Whenever a steamship carrying tea, paper, bamboo shoots, rice, vermicelli, salt, or other goods passed by, they would seize the ship and unload the cargo. Within ten days, over twenty steamships were seized, and cargo worth five to six hundred thousand yuan was unloaded. Steamship merchants, unable to conduct business freely, initiated a general strike on April 11th, which continues to this day. Transportation on the Min River has been almost completely disrupted. This has had a particularly severe impact on the seasonal transport of goods to the province and the city. The Steamship Association has dispatched representatives to Beijing to petition for the right to transport goods freely. Various merchant guilds have also submitted petitions to party and government authorities, stating that the freight rates for sailing ships are expensive, the journey is slow, and the risks along the way are high, making them inferior to the convenience of steamships. They request permission for merchants to freely hire ships to transport goods, aligning with the principles of progress. However, the issue of how to provide relief to the livelihoods of thousands of boatmen urgently needs to be resolved. (April 18th)

Famine in Qiongya, Guangdong Province: Famine Victims Gather in Groups to Plunder Food; Local Organizations Call for Relief 96

Guangzhou Correspondence: Qiongya, Guangdong Province, is originally an area rich in natural resources and products. However, due to the government's failure to develop it and the years of Communist banditry, the political situation and local economy are impoverished. Fortunately, there are many overseas Chinese who remit a considerable amount of money each year, which helps to support the region's economy. However, in recent years, the economy of Southeast Asia has declined, and unemployed overseas Chinese have returned to their hometowns in droves, severely impacting the social economy. Last year, the region was hit by a typhoon, destroying all crops. This year, it has been struck by a rare drought, resulting in missed spring plowing. As a result, farmers in various counties have been selling their wives and children. Some have even gathered in groups to loot food. In the fourth district of Qiongshan County, a village of farmers, carrying their wives and children, have gone out to beg for food, totaling 300 people. These famine victims enter farms and dig up taro, potatoes, and other miscellaneous grains to fill their stomachs, which is a tragic situation. The Haikou Chamber of Commerce, witnessing this situation, sent a telegram yesterday to appeal to the authorities for relief. The original telegram stated: "Guangzhou sends to the Commander-in-Chief of the First Army Group,"

"Chen, Provincial Chairman Lin Diaojian, the famine in Qiongya is worsening day by day, and deaths are occurring in succession. Some gather in groups to loot food, affecting public security. Beg to allocate funds urgently to the Pacification Committee for distribution to various counties for relief. Extremely urgent, awaiting orders. Haikou Chamber of Commerce Chairman Tang Pin San, bows." Another telegram from Li Zuoxin, County Magistrate of Chengmai County, Qiong Prefecture, and Wang Dinghua, Commander of the Defense Corps, to the Provincial Government and Headquarters stated, "Chengmai suffered a severe wind disaster last year, resulting in a very poor harvest. This year's rare drought has resulted in the failure of miscellaneous grains. Starving people have no one to turn to and frequently rush to fields to forcibly take food, and the owners are unable to stop them. Many have even forcibly entered homes to beg for food and refuse to leave, especially in the first, second, and fifth districts. Zuoxin has already used the warehouse donation to supervise the chamber of commerce in raising more than a thousand yuan to first handle Ping County and has separately submitted applications for the allocation of funds. In desperation, I beg your Excellency to grant approval to temporarily allocate 20,000 silver dollars from the provincial treasury or other relief funds to the county, to be kept by the committee composed of legal institutions, and to purchase rice grains and miscellaneous grains on a daily basis for subsidized sale and relief. If approved, please telegraph the Haikou branch of the treasury to allocate the funds nearby to avoid delay. This loan will still be made up by the local management committee and returned in full in August." However, it is not yet known whether Chen Jitang and others will generously provide relief. (April 17th)

Jiangxi Province: South-Guang Highway to Be Completed - Guangchang Can Be Recovered Soon 97

Ganzhou Correspondence: Jiangxi Province is full of mountains and deep valleys, so bandits can hide in them. It is because the roads are blocked and transportation is inconvenient that it is difficult to supply the army in the crusade, so it has not been possible to clear up the effect as soon as possible. Since the completion of highways in various places one after another, transportation is convenient, transportation is fast, and one place is built in one place, and then the key points are selected to build carvings for defense. Now the bandits have no foothold. Last month, after Chen Cheng's troops in the North Road Army won a great victory in the Battle of Baishe, they prepared to continue to advance and directly attack the bandits' den, so the divisions of the 18th Army quickly took on the task of constructing the entire section of the road from Nanfeng Station through Beimen to Baishe, which is 60 Chinese miles long. In addition, Army Commander Luo Zhuoying personally supervised the officers and soldiers to build the road in the rain, which was very hard. In less than a week, the entire project was completed and can be opened to traffic. It is said that the army will continue to advance in the short term, and Guangchang, which the bandits regard as a lifeline, can be recovered soon.

Songjiang: Maojiabang Bandits Extort Huge Sums of Money 98

Xiaokunshan, in the ninth district of the county, is close to the Mao River and borders Qingpu. Bandits often appear. The other day, Wang Huankun, the district chief of the ninth district, reported that several bandit ships were found in Qing territory, carrying 40 or 50 bandits, all armed. Afraid that they would flee into the country, people were panicked. He specially called the county government to ask for the dispatch of police teams to the countryside to block them. The county government immediately sent a platoon of police and two patrol boats of the water patrol team to leave in different directions, arriving at the border that night and stationed there. Later, it was found that Maojiabang, a small town, was invaded by a large group of bandits, who threatened to loot. Later, the town merchants raised funds to pay for their lives, avoiding looting. It is said that the amount reached 1,500 yuan. Since the cash could not be collected immediately, term promissory notes were issued for payment, and the bandits set sail and left. Fortunately, they did not enter Song territory, so Xiaokunshan and its surroundings were as peaceful as ever.

Xi Wu: Examination of Automobile Drivers in the Province 102

In order to rectify road traffic and ensure the safety of travelers, the Highway Administration Office of the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Construction plans to hold a general examination of automobile drivers in the province. All automobile companies, shops, homes, organs, and schools within the province that have automobiles, their automobile drivers, whether employed or owners with driving skills, should follow the regulations of the province's Provisional Regulations for Managing Automobile Drivers and the office's regulations for examining drivers, and from now on, go to the examination locations to await examination, in order to be issued a license. Anyone who has not been examined and issued a license shall not drive an automobile within the province. After passing the examination, the office will first issue a temporary license. After one month, if there are no errors or violations, a unified license for the five provinces and cities will be issued. The seven counties of Jiangyin, Wuxi, Wujin, Yixing, Wuxian, Changshu, and Wujiang are scheduled to be examined in Wuxi from April 28 to May 7, and the results will be announced on May 8.

The Jiangsu Provincial Farmers Bank has recently established a farm produce sales and transportation office, and its business is developing rapidly and its results are excellent. It is now proposed to organize a large-scale cotton production, sales, and transportation office in Changyinsha, where the three counties meet. The method will be handled in accordance with the Farm Transport Office, and the province will instruct the county to inform.

Three Families Robbed by Bandits in the Fourth District 105

Xitangqiao, in the fourth district of this county, has been the site of robberies in the recent three months. The public security sub-station in its jurisdiction has been negligent in its defenses, so it has not been solved so far. The other day (the 21st) at midnight, the Yuan family, an uncle and nephew, and the Xiao family in Shifangqiao, less than a mile from Tangqiao Town, were robbed at the same time in the Waxieba area. One of the Xiao family members was injured. The total loss of the three families reached more than 2,000 yuan. There were a total of nine robbers, who fled along the river after the robbery. The Sixth Public Security Sub-Station of the District has followed the usual practice of surveying and reporting.

Wujiang: Expansion of the Fourth District Defense Corps 106

The Lilli Defense Corps in the fourth district of this county has been making progress since it was founded by Ling Yingzhen and Ni Weinong in the winter of the 20th year. It has repeatedly solved major cases. Recently, the Xibing case of Shangdian Temple was solved by the training officer Xu Jianhua, the first captain of the first class, Ni Weinong. They were awarded a bonus of 1,000 yuan. All the members of the regiment unanimously refused the bonus and were willing to donate it to buy guns. Now, three submachine guns have been purchased. Two of them have been distributed to the first class of the first class, which solved the Xibing case, for use in case of alarm, and it is easier to be effective.

Examination of the Murder of Niece Case in Beimen 107

Bu Da, a porter from Jiangbei who picks up and delivers luggage at Lunbu in Beimen of this city, has a niece, Xiao Yinzi, who married Chen Shaolan as his wife last year. The couple had a very good relationship, but Bu Da's second wife, Wu, was not on good terms with Xiao Yinzi, so she was often abused by Wu. Chen went to Sujialu to work as a road worker. The other day, Xiao Yinzi suddenly died. After Chen received the news, he went to Bu's house to visit, but was refused. Chen believed that Xiao Yin's death was unclear, so he specially requested the county government to examine it. Yesterday, the examiner Xu led the examiners and police to the mortuary. After first summoning the corpse husband Chen Shaolan and the Weijia Miao Kangshou, he ordered the coffin of Xiao Yinzi, which had been buried, to be taken out, opened, and examined. First, the clothes were cut off, washed with wine and water, and examined in detail. The examiner found that the lower part of the body was red and swollen, and the inside was broken, and blood was flowing from the seven orifices. It was caused by the shaking of the fetus, and there was no phenomenon on the upper part that could be detected, not a boil. It was obviously caused by death. After the examination, the corpse husband was ordered to put the coffin back. The next time, he will be summoned.

Jiashan: Playing with a Pistol Ends in Death 115

Shen Qinsong, a resident of the Wan Village in Beishitou Village, Fengjing, was over fifty years old. His son, A Si, was in his twenties. For self-defense, he had purchased a pistol, usually kept by A Si. Yesterday, during his leisure time, A Si took out the pistol to play with. Seeing a flock of crows outside the door, he was secretly pleased. He loaded a bullet and walked towards the crows, aiming to shoot. However, A Si's loading skills were poor, causing a loud bang and the bullet to fire sideways, hitting his own head. He instantly suffered a shattered and bloody head, with brain matter exposed, and died on the spot. Later, when the family noticed A Si's prolonged absence, they searched everywhere and found him lying in the field, lifeless for some time. They immediately gathered the family, carried the body home, prepared a coffin, and completed the funerary arrangements.

Cooperation Between Telegraph and Telephone Is Actively Underway: A Statement from the Chief Clerk of the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau 120

The Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications is striving to develop the telephone industry. Recently, the Ministry of Communications has been focusing on cooperation across the entire transportation sector. Therefore, the Bureau has now begun to cooperate with the telegraph industry. According to Liu Zenglai, Chief Clerk of the Document Section, as follows:

According to Director Liu, the cooperation between telegraph and telephone: "Recently, the Ministry of Communications, in order to promote the development of the entire transportation industry and to facilitate the public, plans for cooperation between the telegraph and telephone industries. Telegraph services are often established in larger cities, but the receiving and sending stations in these cities are not always widespread. Therefore, the first step of cooperation between telegraph and telephone has begun. For example, registered telegrams can now use telephone numbers. Telegram senders who have registered and prepaid a deposit no longer need to go to the telegraph office counter to send a telegram. They can directly notify the telegraph bureau by telephone, and the telegraph bureau can immediately send it out. In the future, in cities and counties without telegraph bureaus, express mail services will be used instead. If these cities and counties have long-distance telephone service, the telephone can be used instead of telegraph communication." Regarding the telephone issue in areas with cross-border road construction, reports stating that the one-year contract has expired and that the Bureau has notified the concession telephone company to negotiate permanent solutions are inaccurate. The temporary contract signed last April did not specify a time limit. If either party believes that the contract needs to be amended or terminated, they must notify the other party three months in advance. The Bureau is still researching permanent solutions, but no firm agreement has been reached. Therefore, there has been no notification to the other party to negotiate a new agreement.

Xu Xueyu Will Go to Jiangxi: Since taking office, Director Xu Xueyu of the Bureau has been striving to develop the Bureau's operations. Recently, he received an order from the Ministry of Communications to go to Nanchang because the telephone services in Nanchang have been performing poorly due to various reasons. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications intends to order Director Xu to go there to reorganize them. Director Xu is currently arranging everything and will depart for Nanchang at the end of this month, which will take about four months to complete. During his absence, the Bureau's Chief Engineer, Shao Bingjian, will act as Director. However, if Director Xu has any important official matters during these four months, he will return to Shanghai at any time to oversee everything.

Industrialists Selling Machine-Made Ice Hosted the Press Yesterday: Clarifying the Truth About Disputes 121

Opposing Market Monopoly

The Shanghai Machine-Made Ice Industry Association, believing that some members of the industry have colluded with Japanese individuals to form a cooperative company. At least a few manufacturers, unaware of the dangers, seek only immediate profit and are deceived. If they are controlled by them, there will be no place for Chinese merchants in the ice industry. Therefore, yesterday at 2:00 PM, they hosted the press at the Xinxin Restaurant. More than thirty reporters from various newspapers attended. Qin Xin, a representative of the Association, reported the truth and requested assistance. The original text is recorded below.

Representative's Report 122

Last year, our industry learned that Fu Zhiqin, the manager of the Oriental Ice Factory (Japanese-owned), Gu Fuxiang of the Weisheng Dining Company at the Jin Shenfu Road and Kuanchang Road intersection, Hu Huiqing of the Tongji Ice Company, Gao Abing, Qian Acai, the owner of the Shen He Tai Fruit Shop, Da Bao Xu Heshan, Chen Lianglang, and Xu Afu planned for several months and negotiated an agreement in March. They raised tens of thousands of yuan, of which Gu Fuxiang contributed 20,000 yuan and Qian Acai 15,000 yuan, and organized a wholesale center for machine-made ice on Hanbi Li Road in the city center. It opened on April 16 this year. The person in charge of the cooperative company told our distributors that the price from the 21st of this month would be nine yuan per ton, and from May 1st, it would be seventeen yuan per ton. After Fu Zhiqin and others formed the cooperative company, they signed contracts with Quanhu Ji Dahua, Qiahe, Maochang, Yongxin, Xiemao, and Xin Maochang ice factories to exclusively sell their products to Guangyi Qialong and Yu Ice Factory, providing subsidies. Guangyi received a subsidy of 5,280 yuan, and Qialong received 10,000 yuan. The entire Shanghai market knows this.

List of Ice Factories 123

The names, addresses, output, and nationality of the various factories in Shanghai are listed below for reference: (1) Oriental Ice Factory, Manager Fu Zhiqin, Japanese, Yangshupu Road, daily output 80 tons; (2) Shanghai Ice Factory, Comprador Lu Wenqi, British, Tangen Road, daily output 80 tons; (3) Dahua Ice Factory, Owner Yu Wenhao, Chinese, Zhapu Road, daily output more than 30 tons; (4) Qiahe Ice Factory, Owner Li Yongtang, Chinese, Huangpu Road, daily output more than 10 tons; (5) Maochang Ice Factory, Chinese, Minhang Road, daily output more than 10 tons; (6) Hongchang Ice Factory, Chinese, Miller Road, daily output more than 10 tons; (7) Yongxin Ice Factory, Chinese, Zhoujiazui Road, daily output 15 tons; (8) Xiemao Ice Factory, Manager Li Yongtang, Chinese, Shipu, daily output 17 tons; (9) Xin Maochang Factory, Chinese, Shipu, daily output more than 10 tons; (10) Guangyi Ice Factory, Chinese, Longhua Road, daily output 17 tons; (11) Qialong Ice Factory, Chinese, Kangnaotuo Road, daily output more than 10 tons.

The Truth About the Dispute 124

Our colleagues in Shanghai make a living selling various types of ice with small capital. In the past, businesses engaged in free competition. Manufacturers, sellers, and consumers formed a trinity. In the past, the ice supplied to consumers was sold at a contract price of up to nine to ten yuan per ton, maintaining its equilibrium and never exceeding the norm, directly harming consumers and indirectly increasing the social price index, resulting in abnormal conditions. At this time of national crisis, when the country is in danger, all of our people should unite to save China. However, traitors and evil-doers continue to emerge. The northeastern four provinces recognized the enemy as their father, but Shanghai, a major port, also has shameless elements like Fu Zhiqin (the manager of the Japanese-owned Oriental Ice Factory), Gu Fuxiang, Gao Abing, Hu Huiqing, Shen Acai, etc., who cunningly established a cooperative company. They have long harbored ambitions and signed contracts with Dahua Qiahe and other ice factories to exclusively sell their entire output, monopolizing our country's ice market and manipulating ice prices. They gave large subsidies to ice factories such as Qialong as a condition for ceasing operations. Therefore, various ice factories refused orders from colleagues, forcing colleagues to sell to the trust cooperative company. Since its opening, the ice price has suddenly increased from eight or nine yuan to about seventeen yuan, and who knows where it will end up. The Japanese merchants, who are omnipresent, have completely exposed their actions of using Chinese merchants to establish a so-called cooperative company.

Opposing Monopoly 125

Our industry believes that the trust (cooperative company) is monopolizing the ice market (special telegram on the 23rd), manipulating ice prices, directly trampling on commerce, destroying the livelihood of peddlers, and indirectly squeezing consumers. For the sake of the country's market and the public's cost of living, it is difficult for our colleagues to remain silent. They have formed representative groups and petitioned the Party and government authorities and municipal chambers of commerce and citizens' associations, demanding that Fu Zhiqin, who colluded with Japanese merchants to establish the trust cooperative company, be thoroughly investigated. They want to maintain national rights and ensure that Chinese-owned ice factories resume operations so that Japanese merchants cannot use their tricks. Under the clear sky and bright sun, our industry is temporarily based on our position to serve the country. However, this is an extraordinary event, and our abilities are limited. We humbly request that all sectors provide righteous assistance so that we can reverse this wild tide. We restate that our work involves fighting the trust head-on to achieve a final victory and striving to awaken industry unity to build a public industry for our colleagues. Our industry is oppressed by the trust and will inevitably sit and wait for death. We must strengthen our organization and seek a thorough solution to find a bright path. Our industry is fortunate, and society is fortunate. (A statement was also issued yesterday; due to its length, it is omitted).

Municipal Government Announcement: Measures for Rice Transportation at the Rice Market Wharf; Abolishing the Contracting System to Eliminate Exploitation of Workers; Establishing a Committee to Manage Worker Welfare; Unemployed Workers Are Placed in Various Industries 130

Following the rice transportation turmoil at the Zhabei Rice Market Wharf, the Municipal Government, after consultations with the Social Affairs Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and Municipal Party Headquarters, has issued an announcement instructing all parties to comply with the solutions. The contracting system will be abolished, and a Worker Welfare Committee will be established. The details are as follows:

Municipal Government Announcement 131

Municipal Government announcement: The Zhabei

Rice Market Wharf rice transportation dispute

has been repeatedly addressed by the Social Affairs Bureau in conjunction with the Public Security Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters. It is widely believed that the crux of this case lies in the employment of foremen by various firms and factories without paying them wages. Therefore, to fundamentally resolve the dispute, firms and factories should pay wages to the foremen they employ and should not use the contracting system again to avoid exploitation. This has been approved by the trade associations involved. It is easy to bear the very small cost of paying wages to the foremen. A resolution has been made, and orders have been given in batches to comply and report accordingly. Now, the Social Affairs Bureau continues to report, having consulted again with the Public Security Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters to determine seven implementation measures. They request that they be reviewed and announced for compliance. This government has reviewed the proposed measures and finds them feasible. In addition to issuing instructions to proceed as proposed, this announcement is being made to make the implementation measures for resolving the Zhabei Rice Market Wharf rice transportation dispute known to all. All parties involved, as well as the workers at the Rice Market Wharf, must comply and must not deliberately violate them, lest it cause inconvenience. This is strictly announced.

Resolution Measures 132

Measures to resolve the Zhabei Rice Market Wharf rice

transportation dispute: (1) The wages of rice carriers paid by Hakka merchants are 3.5 cents per stone, of which 3 cents is for workers' wages, paid directly by the Hakka merchants to the workers through the brokers. The remaining 0.5 cents will be used for vehicle maintenance expenses. Other wages will be paid to workers according to the original amounts. (2) Brokers originally pay 10 cash per stone for vehicle maintenance expenses. (3) Brokers will pay vehicle drivers and foremen additional wages of 0.5 cents per stone. (4) 85% of the original wages paid by the rice mills will be given to the workers. The remaining 15% will be used for worker welfare expenses. (5) Other rice mills will pay rice carriers and foremen 15% of the original total wages in addition to the original wages. (6) The Bean and Rice Trade Association and two other trade associations will each send one representative, and the Rice Cart Industry Workers' Union will send four representatives, and the Rice-Carrying Workers will elect two representatives, for a total of nine people. They will manage the worker welfare business of the Shanghai Zhabei Rice Market Wharf Worker Welfare Committee. The planned expenses and budget for future worker welfare projects must be approved in advance. (7) The unemployed workers currently identified by the Bean and Rice Trade Association and other associations as working at the wharf, with the exception of Shi Dengfu, who is temporarily retained and has already found work, and the remaining ten workers, including Yang Zhenrun, will be placed as follows: Yang Zhenrun (Heng Kang), Xu Songlin (Xi Xie Ji), Jiang Detang (Xi Xie Ji), Jiang Demu (Xi Xie Ji), Zhu Hengyi (Sui Feng), Yang Yingchao (Sui Feng), Miao Xianshi, namely Miao Xiaogen (Sui Feng), Wang Dafu (Xie Changde), Zhu Tujin (Dong Xie Ji), Zhang Sanyou (Xi Xie Ji).

Huang Jintao Discusses the Reorganization of the Kailuan Mining Bureau 133

Huang Jintao, Director of the Mining Department of the Ministry of Industry in Nanjing, came to Shanghai on official business the other day and discussed the reorganization of the Kailuan Coal Mining Company. He said that the Kailuan Mining Bureau was jointly organized by the British-owned Kaiping Mining Company and the Chinese-owned Luanzhou Mining Company. For more than twenty years, the Bureau has based its operations on a joint contract and has never complied with the Mining Law promulgated by the government. Despite repeated urging by the government, there have been no results. Moreover, the interests and authority of the Chinese and British companies within the Bureau have always been unequal, which is unreasonable. The Bureau's internal organization has now been agreed upon to ensure that the interests, responsibilities, and authority of the two companies are equal and to comply with the Mining Law promulgated by the government, like other companies. From now on, the 20-year-old unresolved case of the Bureau can be considered resolved. He also said that the recent labor unrest in Kailuan resulted in losses of about 750,000 yuan, according to the report from Kailuan Manager Nelson to the Ministry. Kailuan's current assets total 11 million yuan. It is also heard that Director Huang will go to the United States to inspect industries and will set sail on the "Empress of Canada" on the 6th of next month.

Representatives of the Silk and Satin Industry Return to Shanghai; The Ministry of Industry Has Accepted All Requested Points; The Outcome Is Quite Satisfactory 135

The Silk and Satin Trade Association and the Electric Silk Weaving Factory Trade Association of this city, because the silk and satin transported and sold to Guangzhou were detained by the Zhongxing Company, which was contracted to collect a special tax on imported foreign cloth in Guangdong Province, totaling three or four thousand pieces, suffered a significant blow in this time of utter devastation for the Jiangzhe silk industry. They sent representatives Lou Fengshao, Gao Shiheng, Pan Runsheng, Chen Yusheng, Deng Hanchen, Chen Weiwo, Qian Boxi, and others to Beijing to petition. It has now been learned that they returned to Shanghai the other day (22nd). According to a reporter from the Yu Xin News Agency, the Ministry of Industry has accepted all requested points and telegraphed the Southwest authorities yesterday to expedite the release of the goods. Therefore, the outcome of this trip is very satisfactory. The telegram and the original text of the Association's submission to the Southwest Political Affairs Committee are recorded below:

Ministry of Industry's Telegram to the Southwest 136

To the Guangdong Provincial Government:

According to the Shanghai Silk and Satin

Trade Association and others, the silk woven with

domestic fabrics transported from Shanghai to Guangdong has recently been

classified by the Guangdong Zhongxing Company as

foreign goods, requiring a special tax to be paid, and many pieces have been detained. Please maintain [the policy]. The representatives sent a petition to the Ministry. After investigation, silk fabrics manufactured with foreign raw materials by national factories do meet the provisional standards for domestic goods and are not imported goods and therefore are not within the scope of the special tax collection. We specifically telegraph you to thoroughly investigate and order their release and hope to hear from you.

Submissions from the Two Guilds 137

Respectfully submitted, it is the case that our guilds previously reported that shipments of domestically produced silk fabrics from Guangdong were being detained by Guangdong and the Zhongyu Company, labeled as foreign goods, and subject to special taxes before release. After requesting the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce to issue a letter of certification and requesting their return, not only were they not returned, but an additional three thousand bolts or more were detained. Consequently, merchants from Guangdong urgently telegraphed to cease shipments and suspend business. The members of our guilds were greatly alarmed upon hearing this news and collectively requested support. Upon investigation, domestically produced silk, in recent years, has been subjected to the pressure of imported goods dumping from abroad and the losses from labor disputes internally, leading to shop closures and factory bankruptcies, occurrences that are frequently heard of. Furthermore, after the January 28th Shanghai Incident, various industries have become even more depressed, and the market is in a severe slump. Especially those engaged in the domestic silk business are nearing their demise with little hope of development. Even the farmers engaged in sericulture and mulberry tree cultivation are angrily considering cutting down the mulberry trees and abandoning silkworm rearing. Investigating the collapse of the rural economy, it is not without a major cause. Therefore, our industry, recognizing that pure silk fabrics cannot compete with imported goods, has been compelled to use some imported rayon as raw material to create blended silk fabrics to eke out a living. Rayon, in today's world, has become almost a necessity for domestic silk raw materials because our country has no substitutes and it has the special effect of being dyed in two colors. Therefore, blended silk fabrics have long been legally designated as Grade Four domestic goods according to the Provisional Standards for Identification of Domestic Goods. However, the Zhongyu Company, which handles special taxes on foreign cloth, does not distinguish between domestically produced silk fabrics that are entirely funded by Chinese capital, managed by Chinese, and produced by Chinese factories, arbitrarily detaining them and claiming that taxes must be paid before they can be released. We believe that the company is currently established to levy special taxes on foreign goods and absolutely should not do this. Moreover, since the import tax on rayon has been increased twice, the cost of domestic silk has increased, and export sales have sharply declined. The sales volume of silk factories that are now struggling to maintain themselves is only about two or three tenths of what it was in previous years, and sales to Guangzhou account for the majority of that. If a transit tax is imposed on woven bolts and domestically produced blended silk fabrics, not only will the tens of millions of domestic silk transactions that are sold annually to Guangzhou be completely eliminated, but also the millions of workers and merchants who depend on the silk industry for their livelihood will also perish together. The company's far-fetched and distorted interpretation is pushing domestic silk goods into a dead end. We dare to ask, are there any survivors among the dying silk industry workers and merchants? Fortunately, your association's regular meeting on April 17th resolved that the many donations and taxes collected by merchants are quite disruptive to business, and the provincial government ordered the finance department to thoroughly rectify the situation. This demonstrates your association's great concern for the people's suffering and consideration for the merchants' difficulties. In addition to having the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce separately telegraph to request release, we respectfully submit a document detailing the decline of domestic silk fabrics, the inevitable hardship of using some imported raw materials, and the various reasons why the Ministry's order designated them as Grade Four domestic goods. We hereby submit this document to your association for review and urge you to promptly order the Zhongxing Company to release all the detained domestic silk fabrics in order to maintain the domestic silk business and secure the livelihood of workers and merchants. This would be a public convenience. Respectfully submitted to Chen, Chairman of the Southwest Political Affairs Committee.

Medicine is a free profession that can protect its own welfare and has a significant mission. People cannot avoid illness, and a healthy body relies on doctors to alleviate their suffering and restore their health. Anything that benefits the public is a revolutionary cause. In our country, facing both internal and external troubles, we must have healthy bodies to seek the happiness of the country and society. Therefore, doctors have a significant mission. Even urban sanitation relies on the guidance of all the great doctors. Shanghai is the center of the country, and doctors here are in a leading position. If they can take the lead, all parts of the country will certainly follow suit, so that all compatriots in the country will have healthy bodies and work hard to save the country. This is a responsibility that you should bear. I hope all the great doctors will pay attention to it."

Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association Submits to Zhejiang Authorities for Relief in Cocoon Collection to Maintain the Rural Economy; Requests Government to Guarantee Loans to Money Shops 146

The Shanghai Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association Federation, due to the sharp drop in European and American silk markets and the disappearance of Chinese silk exports, resulting in cocoon merchants going bankrupt, yesterday especially submitted a request to the Zhejiang Provincial Government and the Construction and Finance Departments for relief and requested them to guarantee loans to silver and money shops. The original submission stated, "Submitted for the purpose of requesting relief for cocoon collection in order to maintain the rural economy. It is the case that this year, European and American silk markets continue to plummet, and exports have disappeared. The cocoon industry, due to its connection with the silk industry, even sells at a loss, which is not easy. Cocoon merchants are going bankrupt, and debts are piling up. The silkworm season for this year has ended, and no one has inquired about cocoon collection. New cocoons will soon be on the market. If substantial relief is not provided, farmers will have no way to sell their cocoons, and their livelihoods will be at stake. There is a risk of them being driven to desperation, and crises are lurking everywhere. Therefore, the association convened a general meeting of all member representatives on April 11 to discuss emergency measures. It was unanimously agreed that, being on the verge of bankruptcy themselves, they are unable to engage in further operations. They unanimously requested the government to provide substantial relief. Two measures were discussed and decided as follows: (1) Cocoon collecting merchants should prepare a 20% deposit and request the government to guarantee loans to silver and money shops. (2) If the above measure encounters difficulties and cannot be implemented, the provincial government should issue a general order to all counties, requiring the county government to work with the cocoon industry association or office to stipulate the use of promissory notes for cocoon collection. Cocoon collecting merchants should still prepare a 20% deposit to use the promissory notes, and they must all follow this procedure, with responsibility for collecting the cocoons within two months. With the above measures, the government does not need to provide cash relief, and the cocoon merchants will be able to accept any operating losses. According to the first measure, the government only needs to provide a guarantee to silver and money shops, and the loans can be quickly raised. Even if it is difficult to implement, the second measure, using promissory notes for cocoon collection, would provide a credit margin for merchants based on the credit of the merchant association. They would be able to act cautiously due to their own interests, and with the county governments supervising nearby and with the dared-to-buy cocoons as collateral, they would be responsible for collecting the cocoons within a short period of two months, so there seems to be no harm. Farmers can use this to offset debts to shops, and it can be used as cash, so they will not feel inconvenienced. Now that the government has no funds available and the cocoon merchants are heavily indebted, it is clear that providing relief for cocoon collection is the same as providing relief for rural areas. However, without rice, it is difficult to cook, and they can only sigh helplessly. Therefore, using promissory notes for cocoon collection is truly an urgent measure. Moreover, once cocoon collection is solved, the price of silk cocoons can also be stabilized. This is an urgent submission, and it is hoped that your government and departments will consider the advantages and disadvantages, weigh the urgency, and approve the adoption of the measures. The livelihoods of the farmers and the remnants of the cocoon industry truly depend on it.

Ministry of Transportation Orders Navigation Administration Bureau to Strictly Enforce Inspection of Foreign Vessels; Handle According to the Provisions of the Shipping Law; to Maintain Sovereignty and Emphasize Laws 147

The Ministry of Transportation instructed the Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau, stating, "The Ministry convened a navigation administration discussion meeting, and the Weihaiwei Office proposed that since the Shipping Law came into effect on July 1, 1931, it has been three years, and all Chinese merchants have complied with the regulations. However, foreign merchant ships have not yet complied with the provisions of Articles 17 and 22 of the Shipping Law. The Ministry of Transportation should formulate measures to strictly enforce the law. The conference resolved to handle the case. It is stipulated in Articles 17 and 22 of the Shipping Law that the master of a foreign ship departing from a Chinese port carrying passengers or goods should submit the ship's inspection certificate and tonnage certificate to the competent shipping authority of the port for verification, or the authority should conduct an inspection. However, foreign ships have not yet followed these procedures, which is contrary to the law. In the future, regarding these foreign ships, it is necessary to order them to comply with the provisions of Articles 17 and 22 of the Shipping Law in order to maintain sovereignty. In addition to notifying the Ministry of Finance to instruct foreign shipping companies to comply, and issuing separate orders, the bureau is hereby ordered to notify all subordinates of this order."

Kong Xiangxi, Zou Lin, Liu Weizhi, and Wang Shijie took the night express to Beijing yesterday.

Postal and Telecommunications Associations Submit Request to Stop the Joint Establishment of Postal and Telecommunications Offices 149

For the sake of convenience for the people and saving expenses, the Ministry of Transportation has been piloting the joint establishment of postal and telecommunications offices in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hebei for more than a month. According to news from the Shanghai Postal and Telecommunications Associations, difficulties have arisen since the implementation of this matter in various places, and it is difficult to implement the purpose of facilitating the people and saving expenses. The two associations have submitted a joint request to the Ministry, asking them to withdraw the order for the joint establishment of postal and telecommunications offices, for the sake of saving the authorities from wasteful expenses. The document stated, "The case of postal and telecommunications cooperation has been decided by your ministry to be piloted in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Hebei and the two cities of Shanghai and Peiping from March 15th, merging the business of postal and telecommunications offices of the third class and below, and the principle is that the combined expenses after the merger should not exceed the original amount before the merger. Your ministry has made every effort to carry out this case, and the main purpose is to facilitate the people and save expenses. The two associations deeply admire this. However, when merging, it is necessary to pay close attention to whether the financial resources of both parties will not be wasted and whether business administration will be unhindered. The two associations have received many reports from postal and telecommunications workers' associations in various places, describing the various difficulties encountered when local postal and telecommunications offices are merged. Summarizing and listing them, there are approximately the following points: 1. The postal and telecommunications offices were originally set up in two different places. Now, due to the merger, it is necessary to merge the post office into the telegraph office or the telegraph office into the post office. However, the addresses of both offices are mostly only sufficient for one office. If they want to merge, they must find new premises. It is extremely difficult to find premises that are suitably located and have low rents, as either the rent is expensive (exceeding the sum of the original rents of the two offices) or the location is remote (inconvenient for the people). It is very difficult to take into account the ministry's aim of benefiting the people and saving costs. 2. Most of the original office buildings of the postal and telecommunications offices are rented from private individuals, and most of them have contracts with stipulated terms. Now, due to the merger and relocation to a new address, both parties must negotiate a termination of the contract with the original landlord, resulting in disputes or losses, which have occurred in various places. 3. The postal and telecommunications departments are not under the same management. After the merger, conflicts will inevitably occur in the division of responsibilities, and it will be difficult to allocate responsibilities. Furthermore, the office hours are not uniform, and the complexity of the work is also different. After the merger, the two parties will inevitably hinder each other, and the efficiency of work will be reduced. 4. The expenses of the postal and telecommunications offices originally varied greatly. After the merger, all expenses such as water, electricity, and fuel cannot be managed separately. However, if they are borne equally, it is difficult to grasp when preparing the budget, and when the personnel of the two offices are placed together, there is room for both parties to shirk responsibility, and the expenses will inevitably increase waste. All of these are factual difficulties, and if any one of them exists, it is sufficient to be detrimental to the merger. There are many similar difficulties in other places, and disputes arising in the administrative system and procedures are to be expected. Furthermore, the people in the interior do not need the convenience of the postal and telecommunications offices at the same time. Generally speaking, there are more times when letters are sent than when telegrams are sent, so the telegraph office may be located in a slightly remote place, while the post office must be located in a busy area. If they are located in the same place, they must be in a busy area, but the convenience for the people is minimal, and the expenses such as rent are more wasteful than when they are located separately. The personnel of the postal and telecommunications offices have different backgrounds and different concepts, and it does not seem easy to have harmonious opinions and merge with each other. If unexpected conflicts occur in the future, it would not be a blessing for either the postal or telecommunications offices. In short, the various obstacles that have already been seen at the beginning of this pilot project of postal and telecommunications cooperation indicate that the result will be more harmful than beneficial, and it will be even further from your ministry's aim of facilitating the people and saving expenses. We earnestly request your ministry to make a decisive decision and promptly withdraw the order so as to avoid the unnecessary waste of spirit and financial resources. I cannot express my earnestness and await your orders. Respectfully submitted."

Li Chao's Concubine, Shi Jingxin, Judged Guilty of Embezzlement, Fined 500 Yuan 157

Li Chao, a Hunan native and former section chief of the General Headquarters' Quartermaster Department, graduated from the Whampoa Military Academy. He later resigned due to hemiplegia. Li had one wife, Zhou Li, and one concubine, Shi Jingxin. Before Li fell ill, he had three large envelopes stored in the safe deposit box of the Zhongnan Bank. After Li fell ill, Zhou discovered that one of the envelopes was missing from the Zhongnan Bank safe deposit box. Since the key was kept by Shi, she was suspected of embezzlement. The estimated value of the items inside was over 200,000 yuan. She reported this to the police and filed a public lawsuit. The Second Special District Court found that the crime occurred in the Public Concession and ordered the case transferred to the First Special District Court, with bail set at 50,000 yuan. Subsequently, lawyer Zhang Shizhu of the Public Concession Police Legal Department filed a lawsuit according to the law. Judge Huang Risheng concluded the trial, and the defendant, Shi, posted 50,000 yuan bail, guaranteed by the prominent figure Xie Baosheng. Yesterday morning, Judge Huang announced the verdict: Shi was found guilty of embezzlement and fined 500 yuan. The plaintiff's attached civil lawsuit was transferred to the Civil Court for trial.
