Zhabei Public Bus Company Petitions the Municipal Government for Punishment of Assailants and Compensation; Detailed Account of Driver and Employee Beatings; Workers Request Six Items to be Handled First

Drivers and ticket sellers of the Zhabei Public Bus Company were injured by soldiers of the Security Team at Jiangwan earlier this month. The next day, all workers of the bus company went on a half-day strike. Mayor Wu ordered Wen Hong'en Bureau and Chen Battalion Commander of the Security Team to go to offer condolences, and work was temporarily resumed. Yesterday, the company again petitioned the Municipal Public Utility Bureau Director Xu Peihuang to forward to Mayor Wu a request for the swift fulfillment of six conditions, including a thorough investigation of the assailants and compensation for losses. Their original petition is as follows:

Regarding the company's employees being assaulted by Security Team soldiers and thugs, requesting a report to the Municipal Government for a thorough investigation and legal action to ensure protection. According to the report from the company's transportation section chief, Xiang Ti, at 5:00 PM on the 19th of this month, Public Bus No. 4933 on Route 4, traveling from the North Station towards the Municipal Government along Tiyu Hui Road, in front of the company's entrance, ticket inspector Qian Yabing boarded the bus and found a Security Team soldier named Ji who refused to purchase a ticket. The ticket inspector ordered him to buy a ticket, but Ji refused and instead dragged the inspector off the bus and beat him, causing injuries. At the same time, three soldiers from the same unit joined in the assault. At that moment, a Public Bus traveling from the Municipal Government to the North Station arrived at the scene. Ticket inspector Zhang Meixin, seeing the incident, got off the bus to mediate and was also attacked by the four soldiers, injuring his right hand. At that time, Zhang Tingrong from the Municipal Government's Intelligence Department passed by in a car, ordered the soldiers to quickly take the offending soldier to the Fifth District Fifth Precinct and hand him over to the station chief. At 6:30 PM, Public Bus No. 4932 on Route 4, Song's shift, returned from the city to the North Station. There were 12 passengers on board. When the bus arrived in front of the Seventh District Second Precinct, at the company's stop, a passenger got off the bus. Just as the driver, Zhu A'gen, was about to start the bus, dozens of thugs who had gathered there surrounded the bus, preventing it from moving forward. They swarmed onto the bus and first dragged the shift closing clerk Huang Riguang, who was standing at the bus door, out of the bus and beat him severely, causing serious injuries to his head and chest. He cried out for help, but no one paid attention. He fled, in pain, to the Seventh District Precinct for help, but was refused. The driver, sitting in the driver's seat, was also assaulted by several thugs with fists and feet. Fortunately, bystanders intervened, preventing serious injury. The ticket seller, Wang Shuyun, hid inside the bus among the passengers, but was dragged out and beaten severely. The beating lasted for about ten minutes. All employees saw that the incident was bizarre and obviously intentional, and the fact that it happened in front of the police station responsible for maintaining local security made them feel even more threatened. To protect the safety of all workers, they came to the company requesting a practical guarantee, saying that unless a satisfactory solution was found, they would not be able to drive the buses on time. To maintain transportation, the company tried to persuade them and finally got them to agree to continue operating Routes 1 and 3 as usual. The service personnel on Route 4 refused to accept the arrangement. (The company, seeing the situation escalating, had the general manager Huang Zhongwen go to the Municipal Bureau to explain the situation in person, and immediately accompanied representatives from the worker's union to the Municipal Government to report the incident, seeking a proper resolution. The director conveyed the message to the mayor, requesting a thorough investigation and a quick restoration of service on Route 4, with the Public Security Bureau assigning police to protect each bus. At 3:00 PM, Director Wen of the Public Security Bureau, accompanied by Chen Zhuomin, commander of the Security Team, came to the company, personally inspected the scene of the incident, and questioned the captain of the Third Squad of the Public Security Bureau and the injured driver, Zhu A'gen. He instructed the workers to first restore transportation on Route 4, and promised to take responsibility for punishing the assailants and ensuring future safety. The workers followed the instructions and restored service on Route 4 at 4:00 PM. This is the real situation of that day. However, the Sixth District Public Bus Industry Workers' Union, to achieve a complete solution and ensure future protection, listed six demands and requested the company to petition the Municipal Government for practical guarantees. The company now submits the details of the injuries sustained by the company employees while on duty, along with the six demands for protection from the worker's union (The six demands are as follows:) (1) Remove and investigate Pei, the captain of the Third Squad of the Police; (2) Guarantee the safety of the injured (assume full responsibility in case of disability or death); (3) Be responsible for all medical expenses and losses; (4) Ensure that similar incidents do not happen again; (5) Investigate and punish the assailants; (6) Reply to the above items within five days. The company respectfully submits this petition to the Municipal Public Utility Bureau Director Xu, requesting that he forward it to the Municipal Government to consider the difficulties, thoroughly investigate and punish the assailants, in order to appease public anger and ensure protection for the public convenience. Respectfully submitted to Xu, Director of the Shanghai Municipal Public Utility Bureau.

(4) Another case: Ren Bingsheng, 47 years old, local resident. (5) Fifth District First Precinct: Zhang Meisheng, 37 years old, Nanxun native; Yao Jinrong, 52 years old, local resident; Shen Aqi, 32 years old, Pudong native; Pan Liansheng, 23 years old, Tongzhou native. (6) Fourth District: Wu Haiqing, 58 years old, Anhui native. (7) Another case: Lu Ming, 52 years old, Hebei native. The above seven cases involve red pills and opium. Fifth District: Wu Xinda, 18 years old, Changzhou native, apprehended for white pills. (9) Another case: Zhu Guangyu, 32 years old, Peixian native, apprehended for morphine.

Suspected Apprentice Theft; Private Torture and Beating at Midnight; Barber Shop Owner's Inhumanity Leaves Apprentice Covered in Wounds 159

Chen Wancai, a boy from Jiangbei, lost his father at a young age, and his mother suffered from foot ailments. They lived in poverty. Therefore, Chen was sent to Shanghai to be raised by his aunt, Chen Sunshi. Chen Sunshi was also a widow, and without children, she treated Wancai as her own, cherishing him dearly. She raised him painstakingly, and now Wancai is sixteen years old. She entrusted someone to find him a job, and a few days ago, he was introduced to work as an apprentice at the Xinmin Barber Shop, located at 1216 Xiaoshadu Road, owned by Zhang Xiluo from Yangzhou. However, on the 19th of this month, Zhang suddenly discovered that 20 yuan had been stolen and suspected Chen Wancai of the theft. He colluded with a shop worker, Wang Lisong, and around midnight, they tied Wancai's thumbs with a rope and suspended him from the window ledge outside the third floor, inflicting cruel torture. They used dusters, rattan canes, and broom handles to beat him violently, forcing him to confess. Wancai cried out in agony, his voice audible outside. He was covered in wounds, especially on his face. This kind of inhuman act is not allowed by law, but Zhang and others did not stop there. The next day, they even led Chen Wancai to his aunt's home to search. However, they found nothing. Chen Sunshi saw her nephew covered in wounds and could not bear it. She reported the incident to the Putuo Road Police Station, and yesterday morning, requested the First Special Court to summon the shop owner Zhang Xiluo and shop worker Wang Lisong to the criminal court. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, stated the facts and filed a lawsuit for the crime of injury under Article 294 of the criminal law, requesting investigation. Judge Wu Tingqi questioned both parties and ordered the two defendants, Zhang and Wang, to post 1,000 yuan bail and adjourned the hearing. Chen Wancai was ordered to go to the court's forensic department for examination.

Carpenter Shop Owner Beats Apprentice to Death; Autopsy Reveals Broken Hand Bone; Shop Owner to be Prosecuted by Police 160

Wan Xiaokang, a thirteen-year-old from Chongming, was an apprentice at the Gu Cai Carpentry Shop, owned by Gu Mucai from Pudong, located at 240 Annan Road. The shop owner was known to be fierce and would often beat the apprentices severely if they did not follow his instructions. Last December, Wan was beaten severely by Gu with bamboo sticks for being slightly lazy at work, causing him to be covered in wounds and in great pain. His right arm was particularly badly injured, and he could not move it from then on. He also could not eat or drink, and was fed by another apprentice, Yao Fangqing. However, in the past ten days or so, his injuries worsened, and he ate less and less. Gu, seeing his condition deteriorating, ordered Yao to take him to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment around 8:00 AM on the 20th of this month. The treatment was ineffective, and he soon died. The hospital reported this to the Jing'an Temple Police Station, and detectives Hu Zhiyun and others went to investigate. They arrested Gu Mucai and apprentices Yao Fangqing, Zhou Chonggou, etc., and brought them to the police station. After questioning, the police chief ordered their detention and had Wan's body taken to the forensic laboratory on Feilun Road. The day before yesterday, Guo Wei, prosecutor of the First Special District Court, along with forensic doctors Wei and Zhang, and court clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the laboratory to examine the body. Yao Fangqing, 17 years old, from Haimen, who claimed to be an apprentice at the Gu Cai Carpentry Shop at 240 Annan Road, testified that last December, the boss beat the deceased, hitting his arm with a bamboo head and holding his right hand to prevent him from moving it. The deceased then said that his arm hurt, and he could not eat after that, so I often fed him. Zhou Chonggou's testimony was the same as Yao's. Gu Mucai testified that the Gu Cai Shop was opened by him, and he was 43 years old. The deceased was his apprentice, and he did hit his arm last year, but he later developed wind paralysis, which caused his hand to be unable to move, etc. The rest of his testimony was evasive. To clarify the truth, the prosecutor ordered forensic doctors Wei and Zhang to dissect the body. The autopsy revealed that the right hand bone was broken and there were many wounds. It was determined that the deceased, Wan Xiaokang, died from injuries sustained during his lifetime. Gu Mucai was suspected of committing a crime and should be prosecuted by the police and sent to court for review. The body was handed over to Wang Qi for burial after signing a guarantee.

Zhang Zhuying's Lawsuit Against Zhou E'xuan for Abandoning His Child; Zhou E'xuan Found Not Guilty; Counterclaim Dismissed 161

Zhou E'xuan, the son of the wealthy Zhou Weishi, was recently sued by Zhang Zhuying for abandoning his biological son, Du Nan (also known as Da Yuan). The Criminal Simplified Court of the First Special District Court heard the case and ordered Zhou to post 20,000 yuan bail and transfer the case to the Local Court for trial. Zhou hired lawyer Huang Ziyan for defense. After the interrogation was concluded, Judge Ze Han announced the verdict yesterday morning: Zhou E'xuan was found not guilty, and the counterclaim was dismissed.

Chen Zaishan's Youngest Daughter Sues for Inheritance; Subject of Lawsuit Not Yet Determined; Land Value to be Inquired from the Public Works Department 162

Chen Zaishan, a native of this county, had two sons and three daughters. The eldest son, Jinhua, died early, leaving behind two grandsons, Wenbo and Wenyue. The second son is Genhua, and the three daughters are all married: the eldest to Zhu, the second to Chi, and the youngest to Zhang. Zaishan died of illness on July 21st of the 19th year of the Republic [1930], leaving behind real estate of more than seven mu of land, valued at over 400,000 yuan, at Weihaiwei Road and Tongfu Road, which was managed by his wife, Tang. Tang died on November 3rd of last year. Zhu Chenshi and Chi Chenshi, the two sisters, expressed their disagreement. After mediation, Genhua sold 1.8 mu of land at Tongfu Road for 60,000 yuan, gave 30,000 yuan and a bungalow to them, and settled the matter, stipulating that they should not make further claims.

Later, they hired lawyer Gu Bing to file a lawsuit in the First Special Court, suing Chen Genhua, Chen Wenbo, and Chen Wenyue, requesting that the property left by their late father, Chen Zaishan, consisting of more than six mu of land, be divided into three shares, with the plaintiffs receiving one-third. Yesterday morning, Judge Yu Changzi opened Civil Court 11 to summon the defendants, but they did not appear. The court stated that the object of the plaintiff's claim had not been determined and should be examined to determine the litigation costs. The plaintiffs were asked about the market value per mu of the land they were requesting to be divided, and they replied that it was about 30,000 yuan. The court stated that the land sold earlier was worth 60,000 yuan, so the object of this case was worth more than 360,000 yuan. It was therefore necessary to investigate the land price with the Public Works Department, and the hearing was adjourned.

Notorious Thieves Arrested; Firearms and Stolen Goods Seized; All Three Thieves' Hearing Adjourned 163

Wang Chengying, a Chinese detective from the Kiaru Road Police Station, along with detectives Hua Youshan and Fei Kelun, arrested the notorious Hebei thieves Li Gansheng and Tu Xiangping on a trolleybus on Carter Road (now Nanjing West Road) and Avenue Edward VII (now Yan'an East Road) around 2 PM the day before yesterday. After questioning, they learned that their accomplice, Wang Wenhua, from Jiangbei, lived at 21 Bailu Road in Zhabei. He confessed that he had three pistols hidden in the roof wall of his home. The detectives secretly went to his house with detectives from the Fourth District Public Security Bureau and found the pistols, which were temporarily stored at the police station. They also seized seven large chests of stolen goods, including jewelry, clothing, and alarm clocks, at the Jusheng Hotel, owned by Li Gansheng, located at 87 Bailinan Road in the same district. They also searched Tu Xiang's home at 159 Galle Road in the French Concession and found some stolen goods. Li and the other three were taken back to the police station and detained. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. When questioned, Li Gansheng confessed that he had committed three burglaries in the past year, but could not specify the locations. He also stated that he had obtained the three pistols from somewhere about two years ago. On the 15th of this month, he took the guns to Wang Wenhua's house for safekeeping. The rest of his testimony was evasive. Tu Xiangping confessed that he had stolen with Li twice, but knew nothing about the pistols. Wang Wenhua confessed that when the pistols were brought to his house, he was out, and only learned about them from his wife later. He asked for leniency. Judge Wu Zehan ordered that they be detained and adjourned the hearing for further investigation.

Japanese Waitress Attempts Suicide; Due to Heartbreak and Yearning for Love; Discovered Early Enough to Avert Danger 165

According to the Japanese Shanghai Daily yesterday, Mauno Fukayo, a waitress at a restaurant inside the Kabukiza theater on North Sichuan Road, had been working there for about a year. To achieve practical results in promoting national products, the Women's National Products Year Movement Committee has initiated the preparation of temporary national products shopping malls and national products promotion vehicles in various districts. Rickshaw Owners Hold Representative Meeting Yesterday; Scheduled to Convene a General Meeting to Discuss Relief Measures 168

To seek relief for rickshaw pullers, the rickshaw owners of the Special District held a meeting of member representatives at the meeting place on Lloyd Road yesterday afternoon. More than eighty representatives attended, including Zhi Ziling, Gu Songmao, and Liang Ruiting. The meeting started at 5:30 PM. Liang Ruiting, Hou Shao'an, and Liu Renhe were elected as the presidium. First, Liang Ruiting reported on the Public Works Department's plan to reclaim 2,000 licenses in the Public Concession, and the situation of negotiating the return of the licenses. He said that to practically provide relief to rickshaw pullers, it was resolved to convene a general meeting of members and ask the members to decide on a method to proceed. After discussion: (1) a proposal to discuss the establishment of a temporary hospital, (2) a plan to seek land to build a new village, (3) how to handle the collection of construction fees, (4) a proposal to generate a monthly donation from Shi Cai. After a long discussion, there was still no appropriate solution. However, it was decided that all construction fees would be five yuan per vehicle, and the deadline was extended to the end of the month to pay in full, and then various construction projects would be carried out to achieve the original intention of providing relief to rickshaw pullers. The industry has decided to reschedule a general meeting to make a decision. The industry also issued a notice to the rickshaw pullers, stating that when pulling a rickshaw for business, the traffic rules must be clearly remembered, driving must be on the left, pay attention to the red and green lights, customers should pay more for the rickshaw fare, speak politely and peacefully, passengers should not carry heavy objects, do not carry vegetables, oily or smelly items, obey the instructions of the police, abide by the police regulations, keep the lights bright, turn on the lights at sunset, wear the number badge at all times, carry a raincoat and door cloth, the rickshaw cover should be clean, wash the rickshaw clean, do not park on main roads, avoid hindering traffic, if the rickshaw is damaged on the road, send it for repairs immediately, do not delay, maintain the business, verbally train people, and issue leaflets explaining, if passengers point out and follow, we welcome you, therefore, we earnestly warn you to avoid police punishment.

Municipal Health Bureau Registers Dentists and Denture Makers; License Renewal Period Extended 169

The Municipal Health Bureau has held the annual registration of dentists and denture makers for five consecutive years. Because the number of years has arrived, the forms of the licenses issued in the past and the names of the institutions are quite inconsistent. In recent days, many people have come to renew their licenses, but there are still a few who have not been able to go due to the distance or because they have moved and have not yet been informed. It is heard that to remedy the situation, the bureau has now extended the license renewal period by ten days, until the 30th of this month. Municipal Chamber of Commerce Publishes; Answers to Questions about Stamp Tax; Also Describes How to Appeal Against Penalties 171

Stamp tax is an obligation that merchants must fulfill. However, although the temporary regulations on stamp tax promulgated by the National Government adopt the principle of enumeration, the provisions are too simple. Therefore, merchants often incorrectly affix stamps to ledgers and documents. Due to temporary negligence, they may incur a hundredfold penalty, which is regrettable. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce has compiled a book entitled "Answers to Questions about Stamp Tax" for merchants to use as a reference. The book is divided into fifteen categories: 1. Bills of exchange; 2. Ledgers; 3. Invoices; 4. Tax bills and certificates; 5. License fees; 6. Receipts and letters; 7. Books and gift certificates; 8. Transportation and customs declarations; 9. Real estate and rent; 10. Tobacco, alcohol, salt, coal, and oil; 11. Application documents; 12. Explanation of questions; 13. Penalties; 14. Regulations; 15. Miscellaneous items. A total of eighty items. At the end, it also describes in detail how to appeal against penalties. The book has now been published and sells for 15 cents per copy. It can be purchased from the Chamber of Commerce Monthly Journal.

Extorting Manager of Li Yang Silk Store for 50,000 Yuan; Three Robbers Arrested; Three Letters Negotiating the Price; Masterminded by Former Partner 184

Li Yang and Tian Xiang Silk Stores on Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen, are managed by Zhang Lihong, a Ningbo native. Wang Wenfu, a Haimen native who had been dismissed from Tian Xiang, and Chen Xiaomao, a partner who had left Li Yang, colluded with Peng A'gen, a Haimen native who pulled a rickshaw at Yi Yi Sugar Store on Tang Hang Street, and a Mr. Li, totaling four people. Two weeks ago, they secretly discussed the matter at a tea house near the New Garbage Bridge in the Public Concession. Mr. Li then sent letters to Zhang Lihong, the manager of the silk store, three times, extorting 50,000 yuan. Zhang reported the extortion to Lu Ying, the captain of the Municipal Police Bureau's Detective Team, and Guan Gong, the district chief of the First District, requesting an investigation. The First District Detective Team, led by Team Leaders Gong Mingde and Han Ruisheng, conducted a thorough investigation. Detectives Yuan Haishan and Yu Maolong discovered that Ma Guiqing, a Suzhou native and hooligan from Xiaodongmen (nicknamed "Little Suzhou"), was suspected of inquiring at the Li Yang Silk Store. They reported this information to their superiors. The night before, Ma Guiqing (Little Suzhou) was apprehended on Minguo Road, across from the Li Yang Silk Store, and brought to the station. During interrogation, Ma confessed to being 23 years old, residing at 8 Chunchang Lane, Ma Yao Lane, Fangbang Road, and admitted to the extortion without hesitation. He also implicated Peng A'gen, a Haimen native who pulled a rickshaw at the Yi Yi Sugar Store on Tang Hang Street, stating that Peng was staying at the Dongfang Hotel, Xiaodongmen, waiting for instructions. The officers escorted Ma to the Dongfang Hotel, Room 53, and arrested Peng A'gen. Peng confessed to being 36 years old, from Haimen, and that Wang Wenfu, a Haimen native who worked at the Jiu Da Hua Ke Company in the Old Zhabei Qiaonan District, had initiated the plan. Team Leaders Dong and Han, along with detectives from the Public Concession, arrested Wang the following day. Wang confessed to being 35 years old, having previously worked at Li Yang and Tian Xiang Silk Stores. Two weeks ago, he, along with Chen Xiaomao and a Mr. Li, who were also from his hometown and currently at large, had discussed the plan at the Laohuzhao tea house near the New Garbage Bridge. Mr. Li wrote letters to Zhang Lihong of Li Yang, extorting 50,000 yuan. He also discussed with Peng A'gen to have him go to Li Yang to negotiate a price of at least 1,000 yuan. Later, because A'gen did not go, Little Suzhou went to negotiate. After the third letter was sent, he, A'gen, and Little Suzhou had tea at the Laohuzhao tea house near the Garbage Bridge and then dispersed. He didn't know where Chen Xiaomao and Mr. Li lived. District Chief Guan, considering the large amount of money involved in the extortion, ordered that Wang Wenfu and the other two criminals be sent to the General Bureau for legal action and ordered the continued pursuit of the remaining accomplices.

Thief Attempts to Escape After Removing Shackles; Transferred to Prosecutor's Office to Await Prosecution 185

Hu A Mao, a local thief, conspired with accomplices in the autumn of last year to rob the Meixing Clock Store at the intersection of Fada Road and Jixiang Street, and the Sihui Clock Store across from the Big Ben, sharing the stolen watches and money. He was apprehended by the French Concession detectives and sent to the Second Special District Court, where he was sentenced to eight years of imprisonment. Because he had also robbed a clock store in the Public Concession, he was transferred by the Public Concession police to the First Special District Court, where he was sentenced to seven years of imprisonment. Hu appealed the Second Special District Court's verdict to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. The High Court approved his request, and on the morning of the 16th of this month, sent court police to the First Special District Court to retrieve Hu and temporarily detain him in the bail room on the upper floor of Courts 7 and 8, waiting for the High Court to hold a hearing in the afternoon. Unexpectedly, at 11 a.m., Hu took advantage of the guard's absence and dared to remove one of the handcuffs he was wearing, pretending to need to urinate. He climbed out of the window on the door and attempted to escape. When he reached the mezzanine, a court policeman, number 515, came upstairs and stopped him, asking where he was going. Hu replied that he was going outside to urinate. When asked why he had removed his handcuffs, Hu was speechless and unable to answer. The policeman knew he was attempting to escape, took him back to the bail room, and reported it to the sergeant, who reported it to the Third Branch of the High Court. That afternoon, when the High Court convened a collegiate bench for the hearing, Hu, knowing that his crime was inescapable, declared in court that he was withdrawing his appeal, and claimed that he had an elderly mother at home with no one to support her, and asked only that the two sentences be combined and reduced. The court verified his statement, granted the withdrawal of the appeal, and ordered him to be returned to custody pending further instructions. Hu was then sent to the Second Special District Court Prosecutor's Office for investigation. Yesterday, Prosecutor Wang Ren convened the Second Court and brought Hu in for questioning. Hu claimed that he urgently needed to relieve himself, and because no one answered when he called out, he went downstairs on his own to urinate. He claimed that the handcuffs were loose and slipped off, and that he had no intention of escaping. Policemen number 414, 46, and 12 then testified. The official ruled that Hu would remain in custody pending prosecution and further investigation.

Good Friends in Life, Borrowed Names in Death; The Suicide of a Young Man at the Chunjiang No. 2 Hotel the Other Day; Real Name Li Decheng, Xu Wenxiang Was His Good Friend 186

At 6 p.m. on the 21st, a guest calling himself Xu Wenxiang, 23 years old, from Pinghu, working in politics, checked into Room 20 of the Chunjiang No. 2 Hotel at 315 Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. Unexpectedly, he committed suicide by taking poison that night. The next day at noon, the bellboy discovered him and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. Doctors confirmed that he had ingested two types of poisons, sleeping pills and heroin, and was in critical condition. Details were reported in yesterday's newspaper. He died at 11:05 p.m. on the 22nd. The hospital notified the police, who sent the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home for examination. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Wang Ren of the Second Special District Court arrived to examine the body and confirmed that he had died from poisoning. Because there were no relatives, he ordered the body to be photographed and buried by the Tongren Fuyuan Funeral Home. It is now known that the deceased's real name was Li Decheng, 23 years old, from Pinghu, a doctor at Baolong Hospital. His family was quite wealthy. He was very close to his colleague Xu Wenxiang in Shanghai. Recently, he was transferred by a Westerner to work upstairs. Li did not want to resign. He also suffered from scabies and could not find a good partner. He was resentful and took his own life. It is unknown why he borrowed his good friend Xu Wenxiang's name to check into a hotel and commit suicide. The reason for borrowing the name is difficult to understand. His former colleagues learned of the news and rushed to the morgue yesterday afternoon to identify him. They notified the deceased's brother, who will go to the Second Special District Court today to complete the procedures for claiming the body and preparing a coffin for the funeral.

Guo Luman Accused of Not Fulfilling Settlement Agreement; Legal Wife Han Claims Guo Breached Agreement; Sues Court to Order Performance 187

Guo Luman, a Ningbo native, was reported to the police by his legal wife, Han Yueling, last year for marrying female painter Xu Zhiqing as his concubine. A settlement was reached through mediation by relatives and friends, and an agreement was drawn up: (1) All of Guo Luman's real estate property deeds were to be deposited in a bank safe deposit box. Guo Yonglan (Guo's father, a supervisor at the Ningbo Industrial Bank), Guo Luman, and Guo Han's seals were required to open the box, and keys were to be held by Guo Luman and Guo Han separately. (2) The monthly rent received, after deducting 333 yuan for Guo's father and land and housing expenses, was to be divided equally between Guo Luman and Guo Han. The rent would still be collected by Xi Wu and monthly statements would be provided for distribution. (3) Each of Guo Han's daughters would receive a dowry of 6,000 yuan, to be paid from the above-mentioned assets. (4) Guo Luman was to reimburse Guo Han 5,000 yuan for selling pine trees, plus Guo Luman's legal fees and debts, up to a limit of 10,000 yuan, to be paid from the above-mentioned assets. Future expenses were to be paid only with the consent of both parties, etc. After the agreement was signed, Guo Luman mortgaged a piece of land and obtained 27,000 yuan. After paying 15,000 yuan for legal fees for both parties, there was still 12,000 yuan remaining, which was not divided equally with Han as agreed. Also, when Han's eldest daughter got married, Guo only paid 1,000 yuan for dowry, and when her second daughter, Peiyu, got married, he paid nothing. Han claimed that Guo had breached the agreement and hired lawyers Chen Tingrui and Che Bingrong to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, requesting that the court order Guo to fulfill all the terms of the agreement. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Shen Hong convened the Sixth Civil Court

for a hearing. Because Guo did not appear, the hearing was postponed to a later date.

Letter to the Editor 196

Dear Sir, I was shocked to read in your newspaper for several days about the motor pump industry petitioning the Party and government, opposing collusion among industry players, Japanese businessmen monopolizing the market, manipulating water prices, oppressing peddlers, and exploiting users, requesting a stop to it]. Upon investigation, due to the plummeting price of motor-pumped water in recent years, coupled with unpaid debts from peddlers, the industry will be completely at a loss. If no measures are taken to maintain it, what can be imagined? Therefore, industry players have gathered to form "Xiecheng Hao" to rectify industry rules, temporarily not offering credit, and to separately set uniform prices, which will be observed uniformly to avoid chaos, completely for the industry's share of funds, without any foreign shares. Now, unexpectedly, this has dissatisfied a small number of peddlers, who are using oppression as an excuse to damage the reputation of fellow players. In addition to industry players detailing the history and reasons and submitting a document to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce requesting correction, there is a sincere fear that readers will be misled. I have specially sent a letter requesting your newspaper to publish it to correct misinformation. Sincerely, Gu Fuxiang, Wu Weiqing, Shen Jincai, Gao Abing, for the Motor-pump Industry Management, please forward to the chief editor of the Shenbao.

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: There will be rain in the Yangtze River basin and surrounding areas, as well as the East China Sea. There will be fog along the coast here and the Zhejiang coast. A low-pressure system in Jiangxi is passing through Zhejiang and moving northeast, where it will converge with a low-pressure system southeast of Korea. A high-pressure system is currently invading the Yangtze River basin. There will be northerly to northwesterly gales between the coast here and Shandong. There will be strong cyclone winds in the East China Sea. Reading News

Issue 6 Edited by the Reading Guidance Department of the Shen Bao Circulation Library 199

Contents 200

1. Short Preface 2. This Week's Information 3. Mailbox

Short Preface 201

Regarding the question of how to do a reading report [Explanation of Doubts] in last week's Reading Q&A. Because that does not fall within the scope of Reading Q&A, it was decided to discuss it in this column.

The nature of reading reports can be divided into two types: one is a report on the implementation of a reading plan; the other is a report made after reading a certain book. The former's content includes: ㈠ Did the reading proceed according to the original plan? Were there any changes along the way? ㈡ If it was not implemented, why? If there were changes, why? ㈢ How much of each item in the reading plan was implemented? Which were done? Which were not done? ㈣ Are the books selected in the reading plan suitable? Is the time allocation sufficient? ㈤ Is the result of the implementation of the reading plan satisfactory? Did it achieve the original purpose? If not satisfactory, state the reasons for dissatisfaction and the future direction for improvement. The latter is something like [After Reading]. In this type of report, the following should be mentioned: ㈠ How much time was spent on reading? Was a certain amount of time set for reading each day or did it change, or was it read in one go? Was there any interruption during the reading process? ㈡ Is it possible to understand that book? If not, what is the reason? Is it due to poor writing, obscure translation, or is the content difficult to understand? ㈢ How many books like this have you read? What are the differences between the content of this book and what you have read before? Which one is better? ㈣ What is your personal impression of that book? How much knowledge did you gain? What is your critique of it. The above are just a few simple principles for making reports. If readers have better and more detailed content, they are free to do so without being limited to these few points. We also hope to be given better methods, so that we can share them with other readers for reference.

Also, although the nature of the reports is slightly different, they can be combined into one when making them. Because anyone who has a reading plan will always read some of the books in the plan, unless the plan is not implemented. When making a comprehensive report, in addition to making a general review of the implementation of the entire plan, the research of each item should be described separately, and then the reading report should be inserted. This is more eye-catching and complete than making two reports.

Dear readers, please submit your reports soon! Because by submitting reports, we can encourage ourselves and inspire the interest in reading.

This Week's Information 202

In the past week, we are very pleased to report a few things to you: ㈠ To date, we have received more than 120 letters from readers urging us to establish a reading club as soon as possible. One of them, Mr. Wu Liyuan, has put forward a detailed plan. Unfortunately, the plan is very long and cannot be copied. Now we excerpt the main points.

㈡ Organization process │ This department is responsible for convening this responsibility, inviting you to participate, and then the club affairs will be handled by everyone.

㈢ The purpose of the reading club is to study academic knowledge and to learn from each other's reading methods. Therefore, it is not appropriate to establish a very broad reading club, but it should be divided into several small organizations according to level, academic ability, interest, and subject. According to Mr. Wu's opinion, it can be divided into three types: A. Lectures on each subject. This is designed for people who do not have a foundation in a certain subject. In this meeting, there are systematic lectures, introductions to readings, and answers to reading difficulties. B. Academic topic discussion. This is established by people with higher academic ability and a considerable interest in a certain issue. This meeting selects topics, prepares discussion outlines, and then holds meetings for free research. C. Reading discussion group. This is the most free and has no fixed topic. Each meeting is a free discussion by everyone.

Mr. Wu's method. Although this department may not be able to fully comply with it, it is considered extremely valuable, so it is conveyed to everyone. I wonder what you think, and I hope you can submit more concrete opinions.

㈡ Many readers came to the library in person this week to inquire about and pre-order the Reading Q&A Collection; there were also fifty or sixty letters from other cities asking questions or even attaching enough postage stamps to purchase it. Now we will make a general reply to tell the people who care about it. The book is priced at thirty cents and is issued by the special distribution department of this newspaper. The proofs have now been proofread and will be published in early May. The initial sale is only 3,000 copies, and it is feared that it can only be sold in this city, so readers in other cities who need to purchase it should send a letter to the department to pre-order it as soon as possible.

㈢ The self-study books that readers have been urging us to publish can also be sent to print at the end of this month.

Chunqiu

The Fragrant Incense and Misty Records 204

— Original work by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Of course, I never reported this to the Empress Dowager later. But I knew they really couldn't get used to this kind of restraint, because such restraints were absolutely non-existent when driving any train under normal circumstances. The first uncomfortable thing was the court hat on the head and the brocade robe on the body; the second was that no matter how hard you worked, you were not allowed to sit down; and third, in order to avoid disturbing the Empress Dowager, it was absolutely forbidden to blow the whistle or ring the bell no matter what the situation was encountered.

How do those gatemen work?

Of course, they are not allowed to board these yellow carriages. They are not even allowed to run over the top of these cars! If so, at least they would be beheaded. │ Then, when this train enters a station and needs to stop, how can these people get on that yellow car and use the handbrake? This question seems difficult to solve, but in fact it is not difficult. Because the speed of this train, from beginning to end, is only fifteen miles or twenty miles per hour, │ roughly sixteen miles, so before needing to stop, the driver must first send someone to jump off the locomotive and run to the half car behind the tender, │ this vehicle is not painted yellow, but is specially for the workers on the car to rest. │ Inform the brakeman to prepare the brake car. At the same time, the driver gradually reduces the speed and predetermines where the train should stop; the train runs slower and slower, the brakeman jumps out of the car and runs to the car behind with the handbrake mechanism, or stands on the ground and waits for the car behind to run over before jumping on, and then uses the handbrake to brake the car very steadily. But in fact, the brakeman has already stepped onto the yellow carriage, which is already a violation of the Empress Dowager's order: but because they jumped up and down so quickly, the Empress Dowager did not pay attention. (18)

Hanshan Temple 205

— Sha Yu

[The moon sets, crows cry, frost fills the sky, river maples and fishing lights face sad sleep. Outside Gusu city, Hanshan Temple, the midnight bell rings to the passenger boat.] The Hanshan Temple in Suzhou, because of Zhang Ji's poem, is famous overseas and has become a famous scenic spot in Suzhou. In reality, Hanshan Temple is not enough to satisfy tourists' desires. A hall dedicated to [Hanshan and Shide], without solemn and majestic golden Buddha statues, is empty, revealing the poverty of Hanshan. The bell tower, the subject of the poem, is too small to allow room to turn around, and the dark ancient bell is said to have been replaced by the Japanese long ago, and is no longer the old object. Kang Shengren Nanhai once became very agitated about this matter and wrote a mourning seven-character poem. It said: [The bell has crossed the ocean east, the ancient temple maples in Hanshan are cold; do not let Fenggan and Raotun swallow it, so that people will never go to empty space again.] Therefore, many of my friends go with excitement and return disappointed.

The most lingering place in Hanshan Temple is a Wangjiang Pavilion. The rooms upstairs have bright windows and clean tables. The Wu Mountain outside the window, with its misty shadows and peaks, flies up to the building, making people reluctant to leave, forgetting both favor and disgrace! This building was built in the early years of the Republic of China by the Suzhou Governor Cheng Dequan with donated funds. Later, Cheng Dequan escaped into Buddhism, and the building also collapsed with it. Last year, the district chief Hui Xinke raised donations to rebuild it, and it has only now restored its former appearance. This is also a small vicissitude of Hanshan Temple!

Small Credit Loans 206

— Hua Ling

[Bankruptcy] and [depression] have become the common catchphrases of ordinary people. In the same city, however, banks continue to open. Banks are powerful institutions; even country folks wearing toe shoes, carrying umbrellas, and wrapped in calico can effortlessly recognize them as the wealthiest type of organization. With banks opening one after another, yet people are still clamoring about [depression] and [economic bankruptcy], it is truly bewildering.

On the surface, it seems utterly contradictory. But upon closer reflection, perhaps it signifies a profound crisis. Those who owe money rely on it to circulate funds and reap the benefits. But with the market being so poor, who would willingly leverage a money lender's funds to pursue uncertain ventures? So, money lenders, flush with cash but lacking demand, are turning to investment in banking as an outlet.

In reality, even opening a bank doesn't guarantee great prospects. Look, all the banks are emulating restaurants by selling "side dishes," engaging in "small credit loans." No, actually, it can't even be called "side dishes"; it's practically "economic set meals." A returned student, or to be more practical, a university graduate, should at least teach in a middle school even if they're utterly penniless and stuck sitting on the sidelines. But if they can't squeeze into a middle school and stoop to teaching at an elementary school, isn't that a waste of talent, and very pitiful? Banks offering "small credit loans" is the same situation.

Therefore, we must acknowledge that the common catchphrases, "depression" and "economic bankruptcy," are indeed justified.

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 207

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 27: Secret News of a Grieving Wife, Appreciable Kindness, Old Affairs Arise After Drunkenness, Difficult to Forget

Two countries. To contend for survival, Country A spent a lot of military expenses to invade Country B, and Country B had no choice but to spend a lot of military expenses to resist Country A. If both sides did not spend this money and sought survival for mankind, wouldn't it be more direct and simple? Moreover, war may not necessarily solve the problem of survival. Countries that were terrible before the European War are still terrible. Even countries that can be self-sufficient are panicking after the war. The great politicians, great military experts, great scientists, and writers in the world must have insights that exceed mine many times over. Why don't they consider this point? Perhaps my level is not enough to understand what war means? Ji Zhi kept setting many questions to embarrass himself, but he couldn't answer any of them. After thinking for a long time, the alcohol rose, and he felt very thirsty, so he found a pot of boiling water in the kitchen and made a pot of strong tea. He packed up the hot pot and carried a pot of hot tea to continue his fantasy. He continued to think, if a person like me is not very satisfied with the war, how is Yang Guizhi different from other women, but she married Zhao Ziqiang, who was fighting outside the fortress? If she did it for vanity, when she wanted to marry me before, she repeatedly expressed that poverty was not a problem, and she also blamed me for only valuing the job and undervaluing love, and for not having the courage to get rid of family pressure. Looking at it this way, she definitely didn't marry him just because Zhao Ziqiang was a company commander. There may be other reasons for this. You can see that five days after their marriage, her husband went out. She can be content with her fate, which really values love. I have definitely read more books than Zhao Ziqiang, and my insights are also a step higher than Zhao Ziqiang, but I am not as good as him in winning Guizhi's favor. (369)

Yellow Wall Foot 208

— Tian Hu

One day, while walking on the road with a Western friend, he saw the urinal on the side of the road and said with emotion: [The Chinese people's abilities are not weak, which can be seen from this yellow wall foot.]

This Western friend later declared to me that when he said this, he did not mean to be sarcastic, but he really said this from a real feeling. He said that with your intelligence, you will definitely be able to understand what I mean. Although I understood what he meant, I still couldn't get a word in, so I had to change the subject for the subsequent conversation. Although I have never been abroad, I don't think there is such a thing as a yellow wall foot abroad, right? Perhaps only our noble country has this kind of inferior nature.

On the road, I feel that my lower body is a little swollen, and I can open my crotch at any time and anywhere to relieve myself. I have to admit that this is our characteristic, and when it is convenient, there is absolutely no concept of elegance or inelegance. In general, the name is called very elegantly, called defecation and urination, so it has become a trend of being convenient everywhere.

Therefore, walking on the road with friends, you can be casual and convenient, and more conveniently, each person does his own thing. The upper part is talking endlessly, and the remaining drops are about to be exhausted, swaying rhythmically. Perhaps only our noble compatriots can enjoy this kind of charm?

What is a pity is that the situation of the yellow wall foot shows that the Chinese people are a nation beyond freedom, and the inferior nature of regarding many things as mere formalities is more important. For example, under the revelation of [No Urination], the [subconscious mind that one can relieve oneself here has become a universal psychology.]

A Moustache Exchanges for Four Hundred and Sixty Yuan 209

— Wang Shouqiu

Roughly a few years ago, a funny incident happened in Huai'an County: An adjutant under a certain warlord went to a barber shop to get a haircut because his hair was long. It happened that this barber was thinking something odd, and carelessly shaved off the adjutant's beard. In the warlord era, soldiers were picking bones in eggs and looking for trouble even when there was nothing to do, not to mention that this was a justified and righteous reason, so naturally they would be furious. At that time, the old man in the barber shop saw that the barber had already moved the earth on the head of Tai Sui; he had stroked the tiger's whiskers; he was also panic-stricken and begged for mercy in every possible way, and also brought out people with face to mediate. In the end, only four hundred and sixty yuan were given to the adjutant, and the matter was settled. There is a joke in Yangzhou, called [one beard for five dou of rice], which calculates that this adjutant's beard, or more than one beard for five dou of rice.

Odd Jobs 210

Study of Inkstones (20) (9) 211

— Bored Guest

▲Other Famous Inkstones▲

3. Red Silk Inkstone

The value of Red Silk Inkstone Red Silk Inkstone stone is produced in Qingzhou, Shandong. The Tang Dynasty record says: [Stone craftsman Su Huaiyu said, forty miles west of the state, the mountain turns upwards, more than five hundred steps, there is a cave that can barely accommodate one person. A large stone leans and hangs in front of the cave. The stone grows on both walls of the cave, blue and red above and below. There are several layers of stone in the middle, with red-yellow colors like silk. The mouth of the cave is a cliff, engraved with eight characters recording the stone quarrying in the Tang Zhonghe years. Su Gong obtained stones of four or five inches at that time, brought them back and polished them. The texture was delicate, the sound was clear, the ink rose floating, steaming and moist like dew, different from other stones. One day, the stone door of the cave collapsed and was cut off.] After that, from the Song and Yuan Dynasties to the Ming and Qing Dynasties, excavations were repeatedly carried out, but no good stones were found. In the late Qing Dynasty, Prince Konoe of Japan sold treasures, including an ancient Red Silk Stone Monkey Face Inkstone obtained by envoys during the Tang Dynasty, which was sold for tens of thousands of gold. Therefore, enthusiasts of inkstones like Toyotsugu Wada were shocked by the name of Red Silk Stone and telegraphed Dr. Ogawa, a railway engineer in Qingdao, to investigate the original site of the Red Silk Stone pit. Ogawa immediately assigned many people to search in all directions, but no one knew where it was. At that time, Mr. Bando was in Qingdao and also invited more than a dozen Qingdao inkstone friends to inquire about the discovery site of Red Silk Stone. Then, according to the map, they found the original pit of the Tang Dynasty, which had been sealed and could not be mined. Moreover, the dangerous stones at the entrance of the cave overlapped, making it impossible to start. They then tried to excavate from below and obtained several pieces of Red Silk Stone, all of which were smooth and could not produce ink. Later, they learned that there was a Mo Mountain six or seven miles west of Qingzhou, about five or six hundred feet high, with a small temple on it called Red Silk Temple. Next to it was a hidden cave with the words Red Silk Cave written on the stone at the entrance of the cave. The entrance was covered by soil and stones. The workers were gathered to dig open the soil and stones, and they saw a wide field of seventy or eighty zhang. The soil inside the cave was red and damp, and all around were rocks. They were dug and tested, and they were all rough. After digging for three days and nights, only a few square feet of stone were obtained. Although they were relatively moist, they had no edges, so they were also smooth and could not produce ink. From this, it can be seen that the reason why the ancients sealed the quarry was because there were no good stones. The less stone that was produced, the more it was valued. Tang Yanyou said that Red Silk Stone has fat veins and helps ink light, calling it the best in the world. Cai Junmo said that Red Silk ink production is better than Duan. Although Dongpo said it was too much, all the scholars at that time praised it unanimously. Huang Shuyong's poem, silver hooks scattered on peach blossom paper, ivory bed grinds red silk inkstone, Wang Yanzhang's inscription, the red skin of the Taoist priest of Caxia, faintly shows veins of chaotic red silk, a thousand years of undefeated firmness and nourishment, who can bear to break its body, it can be seen that the value of Red Silk Inkstone at that time was really not lower than the green stone of Taohe.

Peking League Champion Suffers Another Setback, Zhongyuan Loses to Fudan 216

Thirty-Seven to Thirty-Five, a Difference of Two Points

Jiang University Champion Gains Momentum in the Second Half

The China Academy team, the Peking basketball champion, lost to the Fudan University team, the Jiang University champion, by two points last night. The score was 37 to 35. The situation was tense and the atmosphere was warm. The Fudan basketball room was crowded with people. In the first half, Zhongyuan took the lead with a score of 20 to 1. Unexpectedly, in the second half, Fudan worked hard to counterattack, and the situation changed dramatically. Zhongyuan finally lost. Chen Zongqi and Zhang Jinxiang, the two guards of Fudan, worked especially hard and contributed greatly. Zhang Jinxiang's two long shots were the key to victory. The battle situation is recorded as follows:

Zhongyuan Takes the Lead 217

Zhongyuan has been intense for several days and is not without fatigue. Last night, coupled with the popularity and enthusiasm, the shouts shook the house. Its failure may also have an impact. However, its rapid dribbling and skillful passing have been appreciated by all. In the first half, Zhongyuan took the lead all the way and unexpectedly failed in the second half.

Qiu Guangxie made the first free throw. Zhang Yucai scored consecutive shots, and Duan Zhuojin added the icing on the cake. Zhongyuan created a superior situation of eight to one. Zhao Zhenji continued to work hard, making it sixteen to five. This was Zhongyuan's golden age. Zhou Dayun scored three consecutive times at this time, gradually catching up with eleven to nineteen. Zhao Zhenji added another point, making the first half twenty to eleven.

Fudan Pursues Closely 218

At the beginning of the second half, Fudan suddenly gained momentum. Zhou Dayun scored twice in the right corner, adding four points. Although Zhang and Zhao of Zhongyuan also scored two shots, Qiu Guangxie and Zhang Jinxiang added four points. Not only that, Fudan's offensive suddenly became fierce. Chen Zongqi advanced from the offensive end, which was very active. Zhongyuan was already overwhelmed. The line gradually appeared in a panic. Sure enough, Chuan Xiangrui scored, followed by Chen Zongqi. Zhang Jinxiang made two long shots, and Fudan scored eight consecutive points, taking the lead with twenty-seven to twenty-six, surpassing Zhongyuan by one point. The shouts also rose greatly.

Miserable Defeat by Two Points 219

At this critical moment, Duan Zhuo of Zhongyuan fell to the ground again with an eye abrasion. Fortunately, he recovered immediately. However, he was penalized by Fu Dan for consecutive shots. Zhongyuan fell behind by three points. Duan Zhuo did not show weakness at all, and made two shots. Zhongyuan took the lead again by two points. Unfortunately, at the end of the strong crossbow, Fudan Zhou Dayun and Chuan Xiangrui

scored four more goals in succession, which sentenced Zhongyuan to death. Although Zhao Zhenji worked hard to catch up, the battle ended. Zhongyuan finally lost by two points, thirty-five to thirty-seven.

Must-Read as the Far Eastern Games Approach: History and Achievements of the Far Eastern Games 234

Edited by Shen Siliang

The participation of the puppet Manchukuo in the 10th Far Eastern Games for demonstration purposes has been abandoned. The games will be held in the Philippines starting May 12th. China, the Philippines, Japan, India, and other countries are actively preparing to participate. However, the past history and achievements of the Far Eastern Games should also be deeply understood by us. A book titled "History and Achievements of the Far Eastern Games" has been compiled by sports writer Yuan Weicun and edited by Shen Siliang, director of the China National Xie Jin Association. The book details the history and organizational content of previous Far Eastern Games, including the names of athletes, results of victories and defeats, competition details, and more. In addition to text, there are also over a hundred valuable photographs, some of which are not even preserved by participants. Reading it is like being present at the nine previous games. The book is of great contribution to the sports world. Even the Far Eastern Games and the sports authorities of China, the Philippines, and Japan do not have such a compilation. The book is rich in content, printed with high quality, and sells for only 9 jiao 5 fen. With a preferential discount for readers, the price is further reduced by 10%. It is published by the Laozha Father's Road Diligence Bookstore in Shanghai.

Summer Training Program for Science Teachers in Secondary Schools 238

Ordered by the Ministry of Education to be Jointly Organized by Peking University and Tsinghua University

(Nanjing, 23rd Dispatch) The Ministry of Education ordered Peking University and Tsinghua University, stating that after reviewing the statistics of the student examinations in secondary schools for the 21st academic year, the subjects of mathematics, physics, chemistry, and biology were found to be the weakest. The reason for this may be due to unsuitable teaching materials or inadequate teaching methods. Teachers must first strive to enrich and improve the content and methods of the subjects they teach in order to enhance student proficiency. This task should be undertaken by universities, utilizing all their resources to remedy the situation according to their needs. After repeated consideration, the Ministry has formulated a general outline for designated public and private universities to organize summer training programs for science teachers in secondary schools and has issued a circular for its implementation. The two universities should, to the greatest extent possible, consult and jointly organize these training programs in accordance with the provisions of the outline. They should also select experienced faculty members with expertise in secondary education from among their current professors or hire additional faculty to serve as lecturers and should submit reports on the planning and implementation of the programs to the Ministry for review.
